Abu Hanifa's Training Method: Dialectical Reasoning in Fiqh
Biographical narrative of Abu Hanifa's pedagogical method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe Abu Hanifa's pedagogical method and explain its relevance to the training of a mufti.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa trained his students by debating, exhausting possibilities, and affirming the preponderant view.

This story from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan shows how Abu Hanifa prepared his students not merely to memorize rulings, but to think dialectically. He engaged them in a dynamic exchange where they proposed a refined question, he gave a different answer, and then guided them through multiple rounds of argument to demonstrate that only by considering all possibilities can one arrive at the correct ijtihad. This lesson explores the method and its implications for fiqh training and mufti conduct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the setting and the students' preparation
Note that the students gathered in Baghdad and carefully prepared a question ('amalu mas'alatan ayyadūhā bil-hijāj wa tanaqqaw'). This shows they were trained to produce well-argued positions.
The term 'tanaqqaw' indicates they refined the question meticulously.
2
Observe Abu Hanifa's initial response and the students' reaction
Abu Hanifa gave a different answer, and the students accused him of being confused due to travel ('baladatka al-ghurbah'). He remained calm and demanded evidence.
The phrase 'baladatka al-ghurbah' is colloquial but reflects the students' confidence.
3
Analyze the first round of debate
Abu Hanifa debated them with evidence and defeated their arguments, bringing them to accept his view. He then asked about someone who might claim their original view was correct, and they denied it.
He used reductio ad absurdum to show that if they now accept his view, they must reject their own.
4
Follow the second round: the students' accusation and Abu Hanifa's invention of a third view
The students felt wronged and insisted their original view was correct. Abu Hanifa then invented a third opinion and debated them until they accepted it. Then he revealed that his original answer was correct, explaining that the issue had only three aspects.
This shows his method of exhausting all possibilities to demonstrate the superiority of his ijtihad.
5
Extract the pedagogical principle
The author concludes that Abu Hanifa trained his students to consider multiple possibilities, and many scholarly differences among his students originate from his own teaching method.
This has implications for mufti training: a mufti must be able to consider and weigh different views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخرج ابن أبي العوام عن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن سهل عن القاسم بن غسان عن أبيه عن أبي سليمان الجوزجاني عن محمد بن الحسن قال: كان أبو حنيفة قد حمل إلى بغداد، فاجتمع أصحابه جميعاً، وفيهم أبو يوسف وزفر وأسد بن عمرو وعامة الفقهاء المتقدمين من أصحابه، فعملوا مسألةً أيّدوها بالحجاج وتنو قوا) في تقويمها، وقالوا نسأل أبا حنيفة أول ما يقدم. فلما قدم أبو حنيفة كان أول مسألة سُئل عنها تلك المسألة، فأجابهم بغير ما عندهم فصاحوا به من نواحى الحلقة: يا أبا حنيفة بلدتك الغُربة. فقال لهم: رفقاً رفقاً! ماذا تقولون؟ قالوا: ليس هكذا القول قال: بحجة أم بغير حُجّة؟ قالوا: بل بحجة :قال هاتوا فناظرهم فغلبهم بالحجاج، حتى ردّهم إلى قوله وأذعنوا أنّ الخطأ منهم، فقال لهم: أعرفتم الآن ؟ قالوا: نعم. قال: فما تقولون فيمن يزعم أن قولكم هو الصواب، وأنّ هذا القول خطأ؟ قالوا: لا يكون ذلك، قد صح هذا القول، فناظَرَهم حتى ردّهم عن القول، فقالوا: يا أبا حنيفة! ظلمتنا، والصواب كان معنا. قال: فما تقولون فيمن يزعم أنّ هذا القول خطأً والأوّل خطأ، والصواب فى قول ثالث؟ فقالوا: هذا ما لا يكون. قال: فاستمعوا، واخترع قولاً ثالثاً، وناظرهم عليه حتى ردّهم إليه فأذعنوا وقالوا: يا أبا حنيفة علمنا. قال: الصواب هو القول الأول الذى أجبتكم به لعلّةٍ كذا وكذا، وهذه المسألة لا تخرج من هذه الثلاثة الأنحاء، ولكل منها وجة في الفقه ومذهب، وهذا الصواب فخذوه وارفضوا ما سواه. (۲) اهـ وهكذا كان تدريبه لأصحابه على الفقه وتمرينه على مدارج التفقه، فمثله يكون كثير الذكر للاحتمالات في المسائل، وقد يترجح عند هذا ما لا يترجح عند ذاك من أصحابه، فيكون هو مثير أغلب تلك الاحتمالات، فمُعْظَمُ تلك المسائل الخلافية من تذكير الإمام لأصح الأصحابه.
And Ibn Abi al-'Awwam narrated from Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Sahl from al-Qasim ibn Ghassan from his father from Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan who said: Abu Hanifa was brought to Baghdad. His students gathered together, among them Abu Yusuf, Zufar, Asad ibn 'Amr, and many of his senior students. They worked out a question, supporting it with proofs and refining it carefully, and said: 'We will ask Abu Hanifa this when he first arrives.' When Abu Hanifa arrived, the first question he was asked was that one. He answered them with something different from what they had. They shouted to him from all sides of the circle: 'O Abu Hanifa, your being away from home has caused you confusion (baladatka al-ghurbah).' He said: 'Gently, gently! What are you saying?' They said: 'The correct view is not like this.' He said: 'With evidence or without evidence?' They said: 'Rather, with evidence.' He said: 'Bring it forth.' So he debated with them and overcame them with arguments until he brought them back to his view and they admitted that the error was from them. He said to them: 'Do you now recognize?' They said: 'Yes.' He said: 'What do you say about someone who claims that your view is correct and that this view is wrong?' They said: 'That cannot be, for this view has been established as correct.' So he debated with them until he made them retract that view. They said: 'O Abu Hanifa, you have wronged us; the correct view was with us.' He said: 'What do you say about someone who claims that this view is wrong and the first view is wrong, and the correct view is a third opinion?' They said: 'That cannot be.' He said: 'Listen!' Then he invented a third opinion and debated with them on it until he brought them back to it, and they acknowledged and said: 'O Abu Hanifa, we have learned.' He said: 'The correct view is the first one I gave you, for such-and-such a reason. This question cannot go beyond these three aspects. Each has a face in fiqh and a madhhab. This is the correct one; take it and discard what is besides it.' End quote. This is how he trained his students in fiqh and exercised them in the stages of fiqh understanding. So someone like him would frequently mention possibilities in issues, and what is preponderant for one of his students may not be preponderant for another. He was the one who would raise most of those possibilities. Thus most of those controversial issues come from the Imam's teaching to the best of his students.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a biographical illustration of Abu Hanifa's pedagogical method. It shows that Abu Hanifa did not simply dictate rulings; he engaged his students in dialectical reasoning (munazarah). The story highlights several points: (1) The students prepared a difficult question expecting to challenge him. (2) Abu Hanifa gave a different answer, and when challenged, he demanded proof. (3) He defeated their arguments, then posed hypothetical alternatives to demonstrate that the issue had only three possible positions, each with some legal basis, but the correct one was his initial answer. (4) He taught that multiple opinions can be valid within fiqh, but the mufti must choose the preponderant view. (5) The author (Muhammad Taqi Usmani) uses this to explain that Abu Hanifa's training produced scholars who could explore multiple possibilities, and that the prevalence of ikhtilaf among the Hanafi students stems from the Imam's own method of pointing out different aspects.

Key Terms
تنوقوا (tanaqqawa): They refined and perfected the question; from نَقَّى (to purify, to polish)
بلدتك الغربة (baladatka al-ghurbah): A phrase meaning 'your being away from home has confused you'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was Abu Hanifa's final answer after the long debate with his students?
A) The third opinion he invented.
B) The students' original opinion.
C) His own first opinion (the one he initially gave).
D) That all three opinions were equally valid.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's training method teaches that a mufti must be able to consider all possible positions, argue each thoroughly, and then confidently adopt the preponderant view based on evidence.

Verifying Book Attribution in Ifṭā: The Fifth Principle
Fifth principle: doubt in attributing a book to its author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule that a forged book (kitāb manḥūl) has no legal authority and evaluate book attribution using sanad and textual evidence.

Core Idea
A book's fame does not guarantee authenticity; the mufti must verify the sanad before citing it.

A mufti often encounters books widely attributed to renowned scholars. But fame alone is insufficient. This lesson, drawn from the fifth principle of rasm al-mufti, teaches you how to critically assess book attribution—whether a work is genuinely from its claimed author or a later forgery. You will learn to distinguish reliable critical editions from suspect manuscripts and to recognize red flags like unknown narrators or corrupted texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of doubt
Determine whether the doubt is about the textual integrity (e.g., errors in copies) or about the authorial attribution itself. This lesson focuses on attribution.
The passage covers both textual corruption and forgery; we isolate the attribution issue.
2
Examine the transmission chain (sanad)
For a book claiming to be from a classical author, check if there is a known, credible chain of transmission from the author to the present. If the chain contains unknown or dishonest narrators, the attribution is suspect.
Al-Kawthari's critique of al-Makharij wa al-Hiyal exposes a chain of 'liar son of liar' and unknowns.
3
Assess external corroboration
Even if a book is widely circulated, look for independent evidence: references in reliable works, biographical entries, or multiple manuscript witnesses. A single manuscript without chain is insufficient.
The author distinguishes between single-manuscript editions (caution needed) and critically edited editions with multiple witnesses.
4
Apply the rasm al-mufti rule
If the attribution is uncertain or proven false, the book cannot be used as evidence in iftā. For example, al-Makharij wa al-Hiyal is declared a kitāb manḥūl (forgery) and is unreliable. Similarly, al-Fatawa al-Aziziyyah, though popular, is a posthumous compilation by an unknown collector and contains unverified additions.
The mufta bihi position is clear: do not rely on such books unless their content is supported by other evidence.
5
Document the verification process
When issuing a fatwa, record your source verification. If a book's attribution is doubtful, state the basis for caution. This preserves scholarly integrity and prevents the spread of weak materials.
This step is part of adab al-mufti.

Source Text

النسخة وصلت إلينا سالمةً من التحريف. فإن تبيّن ذلك بقرائن واضحةٍ و شواهد قويّةٍ فلا بأس حينئذ بالاعتماد عليها، وقد ظهرت في زماننا كتب قديمة كانت نافدة منذ زمان و يطبعها النّاشرون من نسخة خطية ظفروا بها، فإن كان أصل المطبوع نسخةً واحدةً فقط من غير أن يتصل سندها إلى المؤلّف فينبغي التثبت فى الاعتماد عليها. ولكن هناك كتب نشرها العلماء بتحقيق و تصحيح بعد مقابلة نُسخ خطية متعددة قد حصلت أماكن مختلفة، فلا بأس حينئذ بالاعتماد على مثل هذه النسخ المطبوعة. (١) وتندرج في هذا القسم كتب لا توجد نسخها الصحيحة، فإنّها وإن كانت متداولة فيما بين الناس، ولكنها مملوءة من أغلاط النساخ والطابعين، ككتاب "النوازل" للفقيه أبي الليث، والبناية شرح الهداية" للعيني، فإن نُسخ هذين الكتابين الموجودة فى (ديارنا مليئة بالأخطاء المطبعية بما يتعسر منه فهم المراد، وربّما ينقلب المعنى. فلا يُعتمد عليها إلا بعد أن تتحقق صحة النسخة.
الوجه الخامس: الشك في نسبة الكتاب إلى المؤلف هناك كتب منسوبة إلى المؤلفين المعروفين بالعلم والفقه، وهي متداولة غير نادرة، ولكن لا يُتيقن نسبتها إلى مؤلّفها مثل كتاب المخارج والحيل المنسوب إلى الإمام القاضي أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالي، فإنّه طالما تردَّدَ العلماء في كونه من مؤلفات أبي يوسف، والصحيح أنه كتاب منحول لا يصح نسبته إلى القاضي أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى، فإنّ رُواتَه عن أبى يوسف مجهولون، وبعضهم كذابون، وقد ذكر العلامة الكوثري رحمه الله تعالى في حاشيته علي مناقب أبي حنيفة للذهبي ص ٥٤: "أنّه رواية الكذاب ابن الكذاب ابن الكذاب محمد بن الحسين بن الحميد عن محمد بن بشر خلف الرقي عن بن بيان رواية مجهول عن مجهول، فلا يصح الاعتماد عليه." ومنها الفتاوى العزيزية المنسوبة إلى الشيخ عبد العزيز المحدث الدهلوي) رحمه الله تعالى، فإنّ هذا الكتاب ليس من تأليفه، وإنما جمع رجل فتاواه بعده، والجامع لا يُعرف. وقد سمعت من والدى الشيخ المفتي ه أنّه محمد شفیع قدس سره يوجد في هذا الكتاب إلحاقات لا يصح نسبتها إلى الشيخ الدهلوي رحمه الله تعالى فلا ينبغى الاعتماد عليها ما لم يتأيد مضمونه بدلیل آخر.
(1) الشيخ عبد العزيز المحدّث الدهلوي: هو عبد العزيز بن أحمد الإمام ولي الله الدهلوي)، الإمام العلامة المحدّث. ولد رحمه الله لخمس ليال بقين من رمضان سنة ١٠٥٩ هـ. حفظ القرآن وأخذ العلم عن والده وغيره من المشايخ ثم اشتغل بالدرس والإفادة وله خمس عشرة سنة، فدرس وأفاد حتى صار في الهند العلم المفرد، وتخرّج عليه الفضلاء وقصدته الطلبة من الأرجاء. ثم قد اعترته الأمراض المؤلمة وهو ابن خمس وعشرين سنة، فأدّت إلى المراق والجذام والبرض والعمى، ولكن من فضل الله به أنه لم يزل مع هذه العوائق مكبًا على الإفادة بمواعظه وإرشاداته وفتاواه من كتبه تفسير القرآن المسمّى بفتح العزيز صنفه في شدة المرض إملاء، هو في مجلدات كبار لكن ضاع معظمها فى ثورة الهند وما بقي منها إلا مجلدان من الأوّل والآخر، و "تحفه اثنا عشريه كتاب عديم النظير ردّ فيه على الرّوافض، و "بستان المحدّثين" وهو فهرس كتب الحديث بتراجم أهلها، وغيرها. توفي سنة ۱۲۳۹ هـ عن ثمانين سنة، وقبره بدهلي عند قبر والده رحمهم الله تعالى. ملخص من نزهة الخواطر وبهجة المسامع والنواظر ٦: ٢٧٥ إلى ٢٨٣)
The copy reached us free from distortion. If it becomes clear through clear indications and strong evidence, then there is no harm in relying on it. In our time, old books have appeared that were lost for a time, and publishers print them from a manuscript copy they obtained. If the basis of the printed edition is only one copy without its chain of transmission reaching the author, then caution is necessary in relying on it. But there are books published by scholars with verification and correction after comparing multiple manuscript copies obtained from different places; then there is no harm in relying on such printed copies. (1) Included in this section are books whose correct copies do not exist; although they are circulated among people, they are filled with copyist and printer errors, like the book "al-Nawazil" by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, and "al-Binayah Sharh al-Hidayah" by al-'Ayni. Indeed, copies of these two books available in our country are full of typographical errors to the extent that understanding the intended meaning is difficult, and perhaps the meaning is distorted. So they are not relied upon except after verifying the correctness of the copy.
The fifth aspect: doubt in attributing a book to its author. There are books attributed to well-known scholars of knowledge and fiqh, which are circulated and not rare, but their attribution to their author is not certain. Such as the book "al-Makharij wa al-Hiyal" attributed to Imam Qadi Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). Scholars have long doubted whether it is among the works of Abu Yusuf. The correct view is that it is a forged book, not correctly attributed to Qadi Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). Indeed, its narrators from Abu Yusuf are unknown, and some are liars. Al-Allamah al-Kawthari (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in his footnotes on Manaqib Abi Hanifah by al-Dhahabi, p. 54: "It is a narration: the liar son of the liar son of the liar Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn al-Humayd from Muhammad ibn Bishr Khalaf al-Raqi from Ibn Bayan - a narration of unknown from unknown, so it is not correct to rely on it." And among them is "al-Fatawa al-'Aziziyyah" attributed to Shaykh 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Muhaddith al-Dihlawi (may Allah have mercy on him). Indeed, this book is not his composition; rather, a man collected his fatwas after him, and the collector is unknown. I heard from my father, Shaykh al-Mufti Muhammad Shafi' (may Allah sanctify his secret), that there are additions in this book that are not correctly attributable to Shaykh al-Dihlawi (may Allah have mercy on him), so it should not be relied upon unless its content is supported by another evidence.
(1) Shaykh 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Muhaddith al-Dihlawi: He is 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad, the Imam Wali Allah al-Dihlawi, the eminent scholar and muhaddith. He was born on the night of the 25th of Ramadan 1059 AH. He memorized the Quran and studied under his father and other shaykhs, then engaged in teaching and iftā' at the age of fifteen. He taught and benefited until he became the singular scholar in India. Scholars graduated under him, and students came to him from far and wide. Then he was afflicted with painful diseases at the age of twenty-five, leading to paralysis, leprosy, white spots, and blindness. But by Allah's grace, despite these obstacles, he continued providing benefit through his sermons, guidance, and fatwas. Among his books: a Quranic commentary called "Fath al-'Aziz" composed during severe illness via dictation, in large volumes, but most of it was lost in the Indian Revolt, and only two volumes from the beginning and end remain; "Tuhfah Ithna 'Ashariyyah" a matchless book refuting the Rawafid; and "Bustan al-Muhaddithin" which is a bibliography of hadith books with biographies of their transmitters. He died in 1239 AH at age eighty, and his grave is in Delhi near his father's grave. Summarized from Nuzhat al-Khawatir and Bahjat al-Masami' wa al-Nawazir 6: 275-283.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage discusses the fifth principle (al-wajh al-khamis) from the rules of the mufti (rasm al-mufti): doubt about the attribution of a book to its author. The author first clarifies the treatment of printed editions derived from manuscripts. A single manuscript without a known chain to the author is unreliable, whereas a critical edition based on multiple manuscripts is acceptable. He then warns against relying on corrupted editions of well-known works like al-Nawazil and al-Binayah. The core of the fifth aspect addresses books whose authorship is uncertain. Two examples are given: 'al-Makharij wa al-Hiyal' attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf – which is proven to be a forgery with a chain of unknown and dishonest narrators, as confirmed by al-Kawthari – and 'al-Fatawa al-Aziziyyah' attributed to Shah Abdul Aziz Dehlawi, which is actually a posthumous compilation by an unknown collector, containing spurious additions. The author further provides a biographical sketch of Shah Abdul Aziz Dehlawi, highlighting his scholarly standing despite severe illness. The key lesson for the mufti is to exercise extreme caution: a book's popularity does not guarantee its authenticity; one must investigate its chain of transmission and the credibility of its sources.

Key Terms
كتاب منحول (kitāb manḥūl): A book falsely attributed to an author, i.e., a forgery or spurious work.
الوجادة (al-wijādah): The practice of relying on a written copy without a formal chain of transmission; considered unacceptable by hadith scholars for verifying attribution.
سند (sanad): Chain of transmission linking the book to its author through known, trustworthy individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the book 'al-Makharij wa al-Hiyal' attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf?
A) It is a reliable work of Imam Abu Yusuf with a strong chain.
B) It is a book of doubtful attribution but may be used cautiously.
C) It is a forged book (kitāb manḥūl) and cannot be relied upon.
D) It is accepted as authentic by later Hanafi scholars.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must verify a book's attribution through its chain of transmission; a forged book (kitāb manḥūl) has no place in iftā.

Verifying Fatwa Collections: The Case of al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya
Warning against relying on al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya due to unknown compiler and interpolations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria for evaluating the reliability of a fatwa collection and apply them to al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya.

Core Idea
A fatwa book attributed to a great scholar may be unreliable if the compiler is unknown and contains interpolations.

This passage addresses a critical aspect of mufti adab: verifying the authenticity of books attributed to scholars. Using al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya as a case study, you will learn why a famous work may still be unreliable and how to approach such texts with caution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem with the book
Note that the passage states the book was not authored by Shaykh Abdul Aziz but compiled by an unknown person after his death. This lack of clear authorship raises suspicion.
2
Recognize the presence of interpolations (ilhaqat)
Understand that ilhaqat are additions not originally from the author. Their presence without clear marking makes the entire work unreliable unless corroborated.
Ilhaqat undermine the authority of the text because they cannot be attributed to the original scholar.
3
Apply the principle to your practice as a mufti
When encountering a fatwa from such a collection, do not rely on it solely. Verify its content from other authoritative sources (e.g., zahir al-riwayah texts, reliable fatwa collections).
Corroboration is key: if the ruling aligns with established Hanafi positions, it may be used, but not as a primary source.
4
Generalize the lesson
This principle extends to any book whose provenance is uncertain. Always check the chain of transmission (sanad) or the compiler's reliability before accepting content as authoritative.
This is part of the mufti's responsibility to protect the integrity of Islamic law.

لا يصح نسبته إلى القاضي أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى، فإنّ رُواتَه عن أبى يوسف مجهولون، وبعضهم كذابون، وقد ذكر العلامة الكوثري رحمه الله تعالى في حاشيته علي مناقب أبي حنيفة للذهبي ص ٥٤: "أنّه رواية الكذاب ابن الكذاب ابن الكذاب محمد بن الحسين بن الحميد عن محمد بن بشر خلف الرقي عن بن بيان رواية مجهول عن مجهول، فلا يصح الاعتماد عليه." ومنها الفتاوى العزيزية المنسوبة إلى الشيخ عبد العزيز المحدث الدهلوي) رحمه الله تعالى، فإنّ هذا الكتاب ليس من تأليفه، وإنما جمع رجل فتاواه بعده، والجامع لا يُعرف. وقد سمعت من والدى الشيخ المفتي ه أنّه محمد شفیع قدس سره يوجد في هذا الكتاب إلحاقات لا يصح نسبتها إلى الشيخ الدهلوي رحمه الله تعالى فلا ينبغى الاعتماد عليها ما لم يتأيد مضمونه بدلیل آخر.
(1) الشيخ عبد العزيز المحدّث الدهلوي: هو عبد العزيز بن أحمد الإمام ولي الله الدهلوي)، الإمام العلامة المحدّث. ولد رحمه الله لخمس ليال بقين من رمضان سنة ١٠٥٩ هـ. حفظ القرآن وأخذ العلم عن والده وغيره من المشايخ ثم اشتغل بالدرس والإفادة وله خمس عشرة سنة، فدرس وأفاد حتى صار في الهند العلم المفرد، وتخرّج عليه الفضلاء وقصدته الطلبة من الأرجاء. ثم قد اعترته الأمراض المؤلمة وهو ابن خمس وعشرين سنة، فأدّت إلى المراق والجذام والبرض والعمى، ولكن من فضل الله به أنه لم يزل مع هذه العوائق مكبًا على الإفادة بمواعظه وإرشاداته وفتاواه من كتبه تفسير القرآن المسمّى بفتح العزيز صنفه في شدة المرض إملاء، هو في مجلدات كبار لكن ضاع معظمها فى ثورة الهند وما بقي منها إلا مجلدان من الأوّل والآخر، و "تحفه اثنا عشريه كتاب عديم النظير ردّ فيه على الرّوافض، و "بستان المحدثين" وهو فهرس كتب الحديث بتراجم أهلها، وغيرها. توفي سنة ۱۲۳۹ هـ عن ثمانين سنة، وقبره بدهلي عند قبر والده رحمهم الله تعالى. ملخص من نزهة الخواطر وبهجة المسامع والنواظر ٦: ٢٧٥ إلى ٢٨٣)
It is not correct to attribute it to Qadi Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, for its narrators from Abu Yusuf are unknown, and some of them are liars. Allama al-Kawthari, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in his commentary on al-Dhahabi's Manaqib Abi Hanifa, p. 54: 'It is a narration of the liar son of the liar son of the liar Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn al-Humayd from Muhammad ibn Bishr Khalaf al-Raqqi from Ibn Bayan, a narration of an unknown from an unknown, so it is not correct to rely on it.' Among them is al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya attributed to Shaykh Abdul Aziz al-Muhaddith al-Dihlawi, may Allah have mercy on him. This book is not his composition; rather, a man collected his fatwas after him, and the compiler is unknown. I heard from my father, Shaykh al-Mufti Muhammad Shafi', may Allah sanctify his soul, that there are interpolations in this book that cannot be correctly attributed to Shaykh al-Dihlawi, may Allah have mercy on him, so one should not rely on them unless their content is supported by another evidence. (1) Shaykh Abdul Aziz al-Muhaddith al-Dihlawi: He is Abdul Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Imam Wali Allah al-Dihlawi, the imam, the scholar, the muhaddith. He was born, may Allah have mercy on him, on the night of the 25th of Ramadan, 1059 AH. He memorized the Qur'an and acquired knowledge from his father and other shaykhs, then engaged in teaching and giving benefit at the age of fifteen. He taught and benefited until he became the singular scholar of India. Virtuous people graduated from him, and students came to him from all directions. Then he was afflicted with painful diseases at the age of twenty-five, leading to tremors, leprosy, skin disease, and blindness. But by Allah's grace, despite these obstacles, he continued to benefit through his sermons, guidance, and fatwas. Among his books: a commentary on the Qur'an called Fath al-Aziz, which he dictated in severe illness; it was in large volumes but most was lost in the Indian uprising, leaving only two volumes from the beginning and end; and "Tuhfa Ithna Ashariyya", an unparalleled book refuting the Rawafid; and "Bustan al-Muhaddithin", an index of hadith books with biographies of their authors. He died in 1239 AH at the age of eighty, and his grave is in Delhi next to his father's grave, may Allah have mercy on them all. Summarized from Nuzhat al-Khawatir wa Bahjat al-Masami' wa al-Nawazir, vol. 6, pp. 275-283.)
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical issue in mufti adab: verifying the authenticity of books attributed to scholars. The author, Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani, first warns about a spurious attribution to Imam Abu Yusuf, citing al-Kawthari's exposure of the chain as fabricated. Then he discusses al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya, a collection of fatwas attributed to Shaykh Abdul Aziz al-Dihlawi. He clarifies that this book was not authored by Shaykh Abdul Aziz himself but compiled after his death by an unknown person, and that it contains interpolations (ilhaqat) that cannot be reliably traced back to him. Therefore, a mufti should not rely on it unless its content is corroborated by other evidence. The passage also includes a biographical summary of Shaykh Abdul Aziz al-Dihlawi, highlighting his scholarly stature and his works despite severe illnesses. The lesson for the mufti is to exercise caution: a famous work attributed to a great scholar may still be unreliable if the chain of transmission is weak or if later additions are mixed in.

Key Terms
الفتاوى العزيزية (al-Fatawa al-Aziziyya): A collection of fatwas attributed to Shaykh Abdul Aziz al-Dihlawi, but compiled by an unknown person and containing interpolations.
إلحاقات (ilhaqat): Interpolations or additions made to a book after the author's death, not originally from him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it was written by a non-Hanafi scholar.
B) Because it was compiled by an unknown person and contains interpolations not from the original author.
C) Because it contradicts the Qur'an and Sunnah.
D) Because it is only about tasawwuf, not fiqh.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must verify the chain of narration and compilation history of fatwa collections; even works attributed to great scholars can be unreliable if the transmission is weak.

The Sixth Aspect: Beware of Fiqh Rulings in Non-Fiqh Books
Cautions mufti on using non-fiqh books for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate a fiqh ruling found in a non-fiqh source and apply the principle of verifying it against the relied-upon Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
A ruling from a non-fiqh book is not automatically the mufta bihi; verify against authoritative Hanafi fiqh sources.

A mufti often consults tafsir, hadith, or tasawwuf works that mention fiqh rulings incidentally. Because the primary focus is not fiqh, these rulings may not represent the relied-upon (rajih) position of the madhhab—even if the author is a respected Hanafi scholar. This lesson teaches you to identify such traps and always cross-check with core Hanafi fatwa works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source type
Determine whether the book's primary subject is fiqh or another discipline (tafsir, hadith, tasawwuf, etc.). If it is not fiqh, flag the ruling for verification.
Works like 'Umdat al-Qari are hadith commentaries, not fiqh works.
2
Extract the ruling attributed to the Hanafi madhhab
Read the ruling carefully and note what the author claims is the Hanafi position.
Al-Ayni claimed Hanafis prohibit ambiguous ihram.
3
Consult a reliable fatwa source
Compare the claimed ruling with the established mufta bihi position in authoritative Hanafi fatwa books (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya, Radd al-Muhtar).
The relied-upon view is that ambiguous and conditional ihram is valid.
4
Apply the rule of caution
If the claimed ruling contradicts the mufta bihi, do not base a fatwa on the non-fiqh source, regardless of the author's stature.
Even a great commentator like al-Ayni can err in attributing the madhhab's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه السادس كون الكتاب في غير موضوع الفقه ربّما يكون الكتاب فى موضوع آخر سوى الفقه، كالتصوّف والأسرار والأدعية و التفسير والحديث، وإنّما تُذكر فيه المسائل الفقهيّة تبعاً لا مقصوداً، وكثيراً ما يوجد في مثل هذه الكتب ماهو خلاف المذهب الراجح جلالة قدر مؤلّفيها، وقد وجدت غير واحدٍ من مثل ذلك في عُمدة القارى للعيني رحمه الله تعالى، والمرقاة لعلى القارئ، ومبارق الأزهار لابن الله تعالى. ومثل هذا كثير في كتب التصوف. مثاله: أن العينى رحمه الله تعالى ذكر مذهب الشافعية أن الإحرام بالنية المبهمة جائز عندهم استدلالاً بقصة على وأبى موسى رضى الله تعالى عنهما أنهما أهلاً كإهلال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلّم. فيجوز ذلك اليوم أيضاً بأن ينوى إنسانٌ إحراماً كإحرام زيد، فإن كانَ زيد أحرم بحج، كان هذا بحج أيضاً، وإن كان بعمرة، فبعمرة، وإن كان بهما فيهما ، فإن كان زيد أحرم مطلقاً، صار هذا محرماً بإحرام مطلق، فيصرفه إلى ما شاء من حج أو عُمرة. ثمّ قال العيني رحمه الله تعالى: "ولايجوز عند سائر العلماء والأئمة، رحمهم الله، الإحرام بالنية المبهمة، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَتِمُوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٩٦] ولقوله ﴿وَلَا تُبْطِلُوا أعملكُم [محمد : ۳۳] ولأنّ هذا كان لعلي رضي الله تعالى عنه خصوصاً، وكذا لأبي موسى الأشعري. فذكر مذهب سائر الأئمة، ومنهم الحنفيّة، أنّ الإحرام بالنية المبهمة لا يجوز ولكنّه خلاف المذهب المعتمد عند الحنفية والصحيح أن الإحرام بالنية المبهمة والمعلقة جائز عندهم
The sixth aspect: the book being on a subject other than fiqh. Sometimes the book is on a topic other than fiqh, such as tasawwuf, spiritual secrets, supplications, tafsir, and hadith, and fiqh issues are mentioned only incidentally, not as the main purpose. Often in such books, there is something contrary to the relied-upon madhhab, despite the high status of their authors. I have found many instances of that in 'Umdat al-Qari by al-Ayni, may Allah have mercy on him, in al-Mirqat by Ali al-Qari, and in Mubariq al-Azhar by Ibn al-Malak, may Allah have mercy on him. And such is abundant in books of tasawwuf. Example: al-Ayni, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned the Shafi'i school's view that ihram with ambiguous intention is permissible according to them, using as evidence the story of Ali and Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with them, that they pronounced the talbiyah like the Prophet's talbiyah. So it is permissible today as well for a person to intend an ihram like the ihram of Zayd: if Zaid entered ihram for Hajj, then this is for Hajj; if for Umrah, then for Umrah; if for both, then for both; if Zaid entered a general ihram, then this person becomes in a general ihram and can direct it to whatever he wishes of Hajj or Umrah. Then al-Ayni said: 'And it is not permissible according to all other scholars and imams, may Allah have mercy on them, to enter ihram with an ambiguous intention, due to Allah's saying: "And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah" [al-Baqarah 2:196] and His saying: "And do not invalidate your deeds" [Muhammad 47:33], and because this was specific to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, and likewise to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.' So he mentioned the view of all other imams, including the Hanafis, that ihram with ambiguous intention is not permissible. But this is contrary to the relied-upon madhhab of the Hanafis. The correct position is that ihram with ambiguous and conditional intention is permissible according to them.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage lays down a rule for muftis: when consulting books whose primary subject is not fiqh (e.g., tafsir, hadith, tasawwuf), one must be cautious because fiqh rulings found there may not reflect the relied-upon (rajih) position of the Hanafi madhhab. The author, Mufti Taqi Usmani, gives an example from al-Ayni's 'Umdat al-Qari, a famous commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari. Al-Ayni, a Hanafi scholar, described the Shafi'i view that ihram with ambiguous intention (niyya mubhama) is valid, then stated that all other imams (including Hanafis) disallow it. However, the author corrects this: the relied-upon Hanafi position is that ambiguous and conditional ihram is permissible. The Shafi'i view is also permissible but al-Ayni's statement incorrectly attributes prohibition to Hanafis. Therefore, a mufti should not accept a ruling from such a source without verifying it against established Hanafi fatwa works. This rule emphasizes the need to refer to primary Hanafi fiqh sources for authoritative rulings.

Key Terms
الإحرام بالنية المبهمة (al-ihram bi al-niyya al-mubhama): Entering the state of ihram with an ambiguous intention, e.g., intending 'like the ihram of Zayd' without specifying Hajj or Umrah.
النية المعلقة (al-niyya al-mu'allaqa): A conditional intention, e.g., 'if I am going to perform Hajj, then this is my ihram for Hajj'.
مذهب راجح (madhhab rajih): The preponderant opinion within the madhhab, used as the basis for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on ihram with an ambiguous intention?
A) It is not permissible.
B) It is permissible.
C) It is permissible only for Shafi'is.
D) It is invalid because the intention must be specified.

Key Takeaway
When using a non-fiqh source, always verify any attributed Hanafi ruling against the relied-upon position in primary fatwa works to avoid misrepresenting the madhhab.

6 min
No Fatwa with Weak or Preponderated Rulings
Stating the rule that muftis cannot use weak or preponderated narrations for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a mufti may use a weak or marjuh narration and apply the principle of following the rajih.

Core Idea
A mufti must follow the rajih; the marjuh is like nothingness, save for dire necessity.

This principle is foundational for mufti adab. It clarifies that a muqallid mufti cannot pick weak opinions; he must adhere to what the authorities of tarjih have established. The text quotes Qasim bin Qutlubugha to emphasize the consensus against using marjuh views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the principle: No fatwa with weak or marjuh narrations except for necessity.
The rule is general; the exception is limited.
2
Understand the exception
Recognize that a 'necessity' must be genuine and recognized by a knowledgeable, skilled mufti.
Not every difficulty qualifies as necessity.
3
Recognize the authority of ashab al-tarjih
The mufti must rely on what the ashab al-tarjih have deemed sound (rajih). They are the authorized scholars who determine preponderance.
This establishes a hierarchy: mufti follows the rajih, not personal preference.
4
Appreciate the consensus
Giving fatwa with the marjuh is contrary to ijma; the marjuh is effectively non-existent when the rajih exists.
This principle is not just preferred but necessary for valid fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الحادي عشر
لا يجوز العمل أو الإفتاء بالروايات الضعيفة أو المرجوحة، إلا لضرورة تبدو لمفتِ عارف متبحر.
قدمنا أنّ الواجب على المفتى المقلد أن يأخذ من الأقوال والروايات ما صححها أصحاب الترجيح. وأما ما يُوجد فى كتب الفقه من أقوال وروايات ضعيفة صرح أصحاب الترجيح بضعفها، أو علم ضعفها بعباراتهم ضمناً والتزاماً، فلا يجوز العمل عليها والإفتاء بها. وقال العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا رحمه الله تعالى: "إنّ الحكم والفتيا بما هو مرجوح خلاف الإجماع، وإن المرجوح فى مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم، والترجيح بغير مرجح في المتقابلات ممنوع، و إن من يكتفى بأن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقاً لقول أو وجه في المسألة، ويعمل بما شاء من الأقوال والوجوه من غير نظر في الترجيح،"
The eleventh principle: It is not permissible to act upon or give fatwa through weak or preponderated (marjuh) narrations, except for a necessity that appears to a knowledgeable and thoroughly skilled mufti. We have previously stated that the obligation upon the muqallid mufti is to take from the statements and narrations what the authorities of tarjih have soundly established. As for what is found in fiqh books of weak statements and narrations which the authorities of tarjih have explicitly declared weak, or whose weakness is known implicitly from their expressions and commitment, it is not permissible to act upon them and give fatwa through them. Allama Qasim bin Qutlubugha, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Verily, ruling and giving fatwa with that which is preponderated is contrary to consensus, and the preponderated in comparison to the preponderant (rajih) is like nothingness. Tarjih without a preponderating factor in opposing matters is prohibited. And whoever is satisfied that his fatwa or action be in agreement with a statement or aspect in the issue, and he acts with whatever statements and aspects he wishes without consideration of preponderance, ...'
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage lays down a key principle for muftis: it is not allowed to issue fatwas based on weak or marjuh (preponderated) narrations unless there is a pressing necessity that an expert mufti recognizes. The author reiterates that a muqallid mufti must adhere to the views that the authorities of tarjih have deemed correct. The text then quotes Qasim bin Qutlubugha who emphasizes that giving fatwa based on a marjuh view contradicts ijma (consensus). The marjuh is effectively considered nonexistent when weighed against the rajih. It is forbidden to assign preponderance without a valid preponderating factor, and one cannot simply pick any view from the school without regard to tarjih. This reinforces the obligation of following the strongest position within the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
مرجوح (marjuh): A ruling or narration that is outweighed by a stronger (rajih) opinion or evidence.
راجح (rajih): The preponderant or stronger opinion that should be followed in fatwa.
أصحاب الترجيح (ashab al-tarjih): The scholars authorized to determine which rulings/ narrations are stronger within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eleventh principle, when is it permissible to act upon a weak or marjuh narration?
A) Always, as long as it is found in a fiqh book.
B) Only if there is a necessity that a knowledgeable and skilled mufti perceives.
C) Never, under any circumstances.
D) When the narration is from the early Hanafi authorities.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must always follow the rajih; using a marjuh view requires a genuine necessity recognized by an expert.

Conditions for Fatwa with Another Madhhab and Avoiding Shadhdh
Two fatwa rules + hadith + warnings against tafarrudat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions for issuing a fatwa with another madhhab and evaluate the prohibition against anomalous opinions (shadhdh) using Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
Issuing fatwa with another madhhab requires rigorous verification and avoidance of anomalous opinions that contradict the majority.

A mufti trained in the Hanafi school may sometimes need to issue a fatwa according to another madhhab. This lesson presents two essential rules from Usul al-Iftaa: first, the mufti must thoroughly investigate the target madhhab's methodology and terminology, preferably by consulting its scholars; second, the opinion adopted must not be shadhdh (anomalous) – i.e., contradicting the majority of jurists. The passage grounds these rules in hadith and early scholarly consensus, warning against 'tattabu' al-rukhas' (following licenses) that leads to religious laxity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Conditions
Locate the third and fourth rules in the passage: (i) thorough verification of the other madhhab, and (ii) avoidance of shadhdh opinions. Understand each condition's rationale.
The first condition is about methodology; the second about reliability.
2
Analyze the Hadith Proof
The author cites two hadiths on the community not uniting on error and the obligation to adhere to the great majority (sawad al-a'zam). Examine how these support the prohibition of shadhdh opinions.
Note the chain weakness of the second hadith, but the meaning is supported by other evidence.
3
Understand the Warning Against Tafarrudat and Rukhsas
The passage quotes early scholars condemning those who pick anomalous opinions or follow licenses from different schools. Identify the key terms: tafarrudat (odd opinions), rukhsas (licenses), and the blameworthy practice of tatabbu' al-rukhas.
This warning applies even when the opinion comes from a respected imam; the issue is its anomaly.
4
Apply to a Fatwa Scenario
Consider a modern case: a mufti is asked about a financial transaction and finds a lenient ruling from the Maliki school in one book. Apply the two conditions: must verify Maliki terminology and ensure the opinion is not shadhdh (i.e., widely accepted in the Maliki school).
The mufti must not simply grab the easiest ruling; he must follow the mufta bihi of that madhhab.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الافتاء بمذهب آخر الثالث: أن يتأكد ويتثبت في تحقيق المذهب الذي يريد أن يفتي به تحقيقاً بالغاً، والأحسن أن يراجع في ذلك علماء ذلك المذهب، ولا يكتفى برؤية مسألة في كتاب أو كتابين، لأن كل مذهب له مصطلحات تخصه، وأساليب ينفرد بها، وربما لا يصل إلى مرادها الحقيقي إلا من مارس هذه المصطلحات والأساليب. الرابع: أن لا يكون القول المأخوذ به من الأقوال الشاذة التي تخالف جماهير فقهاء الأمة، ووقع منهم الإنكار عليها. روى عبدالله بن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "إن الله لا يجمع أمتي أو قال: أمة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم على ضلالة، ويد الله على الجماعة، ومن شذ شذ إلى النار." (1) وروى عن أنس بن مالك رضي الله عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "إن أمتي لا تجتمع على ضلالة، فإذا رأيتم اختلافا، فعليكم بالسواد الأعظم." (2) وقد صدرت من بعض الفقهاء تفردات لم يأخذ بها جماهير أهل العلم، بل وقع منهم الإنكار عليها. وإن اللجوء إلى تلك التفردات طلباً للتيسير وتتبعاً للرخص مما شنع عليه السلف قديماً وحديثاً. (1) أخرجه الترمذي في الفتن، باب ما جاء في لزوم الجماعة، حديث ٢١٦٧، وقال: "هذا حديث غريب من هذا الوجه، وسليمان المدني هو عندي سليمان بن سفيان، وفي الباب عن ابن عباس، وقد روى عنه أبو داود الطيالسي وأبو عامر العقدي، وغير واحد من أهل العلم. وتفسير الجماعة عند أهل العلم هم أهل الفقه والعلم والحديث." (2) سنن ابن ماجه أبواب الفتن، باب السواد الأعظم برقم ٣٩٥٠، وقال البوصيري: هذا إسناد ضعيف لضعف أبي خلف الأعمى... وقد روي هذا الحديث من حديث أبي ذر وأبي مالك الأشعري وابن عمر وأبي نصرة وقدامة بن عبد الله الكلابي، وفي كلها نظر. قاله شيخنا العراقي رحمه الله تعالى. (مصباح الزجاجة ج ٤ ص ١٦٩) قال الإمام الأوزاعي رحمه الله تعالى: "من أخذ بنوادر العلماء خرج من الإسلام." وقال الحافظ الذهبي رحمه الله تعالى: "ومن تتبع رخص المذاهب وزلات المجتهدين فقد رق دينه، كما قال الأوزاعي وغيره: من أخذ بقول المكيين في المتعة، والكوفيين في النبيذ، والمدنيين في الغناء، والشامين في عصمة الخلفاء فقد جمع الشر. وكذا من أخذ في البيوع الربوية بمن يحتال عليها، وفي الطلاق ونكاح التحليل بمن توسع فيه، وشبه ذلك، فقد تعرض للانحلال." وقال الإمام أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله تعالى: "لو أن رجلاً عمل بكل رخصة: بقول أهل الكوفة في النبيذ، وأهل المدينة في السماع، وأهل مكة في المتعة، كان فاسقاً." وقال معمر: "لو أن رجلاً أخذ بقول أهل المدينة في السماع يعني الغناء، وإتيان النساء في أدبارهن، وبقول أهل مكة في المتعة والصرف، وبقول أهل الكوفة في المسكر، كان أشر عباد الله تعالى." وقال سليمان السيمي: "لو أخذت برخصة كل عالم أو قال: زلة كل عالم اجتمع فيك الشر كله." وقال عبدالرحمن بن مهدي رحمه الله تعالى: "لا يكون إماماً في العلم من أخذ بالشاذ، ولا إماماً في العلم من روى عن كل أحد، ولا يكون إماماً من حدث بكل ما سمع. هذا ما رأوه في الأقوال الشاذة التي صدرت من الفقهاء الكبار الموثوقين الذين شهد لهم أهل العلم بالتفقه والورع، فما بالك بالأقوال الشاذة الصادرة..." (1) تذكرة الحفاظ للذهبي، ترجمة الإمام أبي عمرو عبدالرحمن بن عمرو الأوزاعي، ص ١٨٠ ج ١ (2) سير أعلام النبلاء للذهبي، ترجمة الإمام مالك، ٨ ص ٩٠ (3) راجع لهذه الأقوال كلها لوامع الأنوار البهية للسفاريني، ج ٢ ص ٤٦٦ (4) جامع بيان العلم وفضله لابن عبدالبر، ج ٣ ص ٣٥ فقره ٩٧٧
Issuing Fatwa with Another Madhhab

Third: That he thoroughly verify and establish in investigating the madhhab he wants to give fatwa with, a thorough investigation. It is better that he consult in that the scholars of that madhhab, and he should not be satisfied by seeing a issue in one or two books, because every madhhab has its own terminologies and unique methods, and perhaps one cannot reach their true intended meaning except one who has practiced these terminologies and methods.

Fourth: That the opinion taken should not be from the anomalous opinions that contradict the majority of the jurists of the ummah, and they have denounced them. 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he said: "Indeed Allah will not gather my ummah – or he said: the ummah of Muhammad – upon misguidance, and the hand of Allah is with the congregation, and whoever deviates deviates to the Fire." (1) And it was narrated from Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: "Indeed my ummah will not gather upon misguidance, so if you see disagreement, then stick to the great majority." (2) And some jurists have issued unique opinions that the majority of the people of knowledge did not accept; rather they denounced them. And resorting to those unique opinions seeking ease and following licenses has been condemned by the predecessors, past and present.

(1) Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in al-Fitan, chapter on adhering to the congregation, hadith 2167, and he said: "This hadith is gharib from this chain, and Sulayman al-Madani is in my view Sulayman ibn Sufyan, and in the chapter from Ibn 'Abbas, and it has been narrated from him by Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi and Abu 'Amir al-'Aqadi and many scholars. The interpretation of 'congregation' according to the scholars is the people of fiqh, knowledge, and hadith."
(2) Sunan Ibn Majah, chapters on al-Fitan, chapter on al-Sawad al-A'zam, number 3950, and al-Busayri said: This chain is weak due to the weakness of Abu Khalf al-A'ma... And this hadith has been narrated from Abu Dharr, Abu Malik al-Ash'ari, Ibn 'Umar, Abu Nasra, and Qudamah ibn 'Abdullah al-Kilabi, and all have issues. So said our teacher al-'Iraqi (may Allah have mercy on him). (Misbah al-Zujajah, vol. 4, p. 169)

Imam al-Awza'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "Whoever takes the oddities of scholars has left Islam." Al-Hafiz al-Dhahabi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "Whoever follows licenses of the schools and slips of the mujtahids, his religion becomes thin; as al-Awza'i and others said: Whoever takes the statement of the Makkans regarding mut'ah, the Kufans regarding wine, the Madinans regarding singing, and the Syrians regarding the infallibility of the caliphs, has gathered evil. Likewise, whoever takes in usurious transactions from those who practice legal trickery, and in divorce and marriage of tahlil from those who are lenient, and the like, he exposes himself to dissolution."

Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "If a man acted upon every license: the statement of the Kufans regarding wine, the Madinans regarding listening, and the Makkans regarding mut'ah, he would be a transgressor."

And Ma'mar said: "If a man took the statement of the Madinans regarding listening (i.e., singing) and approaching women from behind, and the statement of the Makkans regarding mut'ah and exchange, and the statement of the Kufans regarding intoxicants, he would be the worst of Allah's servants."

And Sulayman al-Saymi said: "If you take the license of every scholar – or he said: the slip of every scholar – all evil would be gathered in you."

And 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "One cannot be an imam in knowledge who takes the anomalous, and one cannot be an imam in knowledge who narrates from everyone, and one cannot be an imam who narrates everything he hears. This is what they held regarding anomalous statements that issued from the great reliable jurists whom the people of knowledge attested to in fiqh and piety, so what about anomalous statements that issued from..."

(1) Tadhkirat al-Huffaz of al-Dhahabi, biography of Imam Abu 'Amr 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Amr al-Awza'i, p. 180 vol. 1
(2) Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' of al-Dhahabi, biography of Imam Malik, 8 p. 90
(3) Refer for all these statements to Lawami' al-Anwar al-Bahiyya of al-Saffarini, vol. 2 p. 466
(4) Jami' Bayan al-'Ilm wa Fadlihi of Ibn 'Abd al-Barr, vol. 3 p. 35 paragraph 977
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents two methodological rules for a mufti when issuing a fatwa according to a madhhab other than his own. The third rule mandates a thorough investigation of the target madhhab—its terminologies and methods—preferably by consulting its scholars, as surface reading of one or two books is insufficient. The fourth rule prohibits adopting shadhdh (anomalous) opinions that contradict the majority of jurists. Two hadiths support this: the community will not unite on error, and one must adhere to the great majority (sawad al-a'zam). The author then warns against tafarrudat (odd opinions) issued by some jurists, which were rejected by the majority. Seeking ease (taysir) by following rukhsas (licenses) from anomalous views is condemned. Quoting al-Awza'i, al-Dhahabi, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ma'mar, al-Saymi, and Ibn Mahdi, the passage emphasizes that picking and choosing the most permissive opinions from various schools without regard for their mainstream positions leads to religious laxity and even transgression. The quotes illustrate that a true imam avoids shadhdh opinions, does not narrate from everyone, and does not report everything he hears. The overall message is that a mufti must be rigorous, avoid anomalous opinions, and stick to the well-established positions of the madhahib.

Key Terms
تفردات (tafarrudat): Unique or anomalous opinions issued by individual jurists that were not accepted by the majority of scholars and were often denounced by them.
رخص (rukhsas): Licenses or legal concessions that allow an exception to a general ruling under specific circumstances.
شاذ (shadhdh): An opinion that contradicts the majority of jurists and is not widely accepted; considered anomalous and unreliable for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the fourth condition for issuing a fatwa with another madhhab?
A) The opinion must be from a reliable book.
B) The opinion must not be from shadhdh (anomalous) opinions that contradict the majority of jurists.
C) The mufti must consult scholars of that madhhab.
D) The opinion must be from the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Issuing a fatwa with another madhhab requires both rigorous verification of its methodology and avoidance of anomalous opinions (shadhdh), as the majority represents the truth and deviation leads to error.

Fatwa Based on a Strong Hadith Contrary to Madhhab
Ruling on a mufti acting on a sahih hadith contrary to his madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may issue a fatwa based on a sahih hadith contrary to the madhhab, and apply the condition of being mutabahhir.

Core Idea
A qualified Hanafi mufti can act on a sahih hadith even if it contradicts his madhhab.

This lesson examines the second scenario in Rasm al-Mufti where a mufti may depart from the relied-upon position of his madhhab: when he encounters a sound hadith with clear legal indication and no counter evidence except his imam's statement. The passage establishes the permissibility, outlines the required qualification (mutabahhir), and traces the authority back to Abu Hanifa's famous statement. It also clarifies that the follower does not leave the Hanafi school by acting on such a fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that this is the second case in Rasm al-Mufti where a mufti may act outside the madhhab: when a sahih hadith with clear indication contradicts the madhhab.
2
State the condition for the mufti
The mufti must be 'mutabahhir' – deeply learned in the madhhab, knowledgeable of evidence, and able to distinguish abrogated from abrogating texts.
This is below full ijtihad but requires deep insight into Quran and Sunnah.
3
Locate the evidence
The primary evidence is Abu Hanifa's statement 'If a hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab', transmitted by Ibn Abd al-Barr and al-Sha'rani.
This is a transmitted qawl of the Imam.
4
Apply the condition to a scenario
If a mufti meets the condition and finds a sahih hadith with no objection except his imam's opinion, he may adopt the view of a mujtahid who acted on that hadith.
The fatwa does not remove the follower from the Hanafi school.
5
Note the practical restriction
The mufti must be qualified to examine texts and ensure the hadith is not abrogated or contradicted by stronger evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحالة الثانية: التى يجوز فيها العمل والافتاء بمذهب الغير أن يكون المفتى متبحراً في المذهب، عارفاً بالدلائل له نظر عميق فى القرآن والسنّة ، وإن لم يبلغ درجة الاجتهاد، ولكنه يطلع على حديث صحيح واضح الدلالة، ولا يجد له معارضاً إلا قول امامه، فحينئذ يسوغ له الأخذ بقول مجتهد عمل بذلك الحديث، كما فصلنا في مبحث التقليد والتمذهب وهذا الذى ذكرناه موافق لما حكاه العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في شرح عقود رسم المفتى عن شرح الأشباه للبيري رحمه الله تعالى عن شرح الهداية لابن الشحْنَة الكبير ) : "إذا صح الحديث وكان على خلاف المذهب، عُمل بالحديث، ويكون ذلك مذهبه، ولا يخرج مقلّده عن كونه حنفيّاً بالعمل به، فقد صح عن أبي حنيفة أنّه قال: "إذا صح الحديث فهو مذهبي." وقد حكى العلامة ابن عبد البر عن أبي حنيفة وغيره من الأئمة، و نقله أيضاً الإمام الشعراني عن الأئمة الأربعة. قلت: ولا يخفى أن ذلك لمن كان أهلاً للنظر فى النصوص ومعرفة مُحْكَمِها من منسوخها، فإذا نظر اسمه (۱) ابن الشحنة الكبير : هو محمد بن محمد بن محمود أبو الوليد محب الدين، ابن الشحنة الكبير الحلبي وهو والد أبي الفضل محمد ابن الشحنة الصغير. وآل الشحنة، نسبتهم إلى جد لهم كان شحنة حلب، وهو ما نسميه اليوم رئيس الشرطة أو مدير البوليس. (الحاشية على الأعلام (٧:٥١ فقيه حنفي، له اشتغال بالأدب والتاريخ من علماء حلب. ولي قضاءها مرات واستقضي بدمشق والقاهرة. له كتب منها: "روض المناظر في علم الأوائل والأواخر" اختصر به تاريخ أبي الفداء، وذيل عليه إلى سنة ٨٠٦هـ، وكتاب فى السيرة النبوية، ومنظومة، وشرحها، و"نهاية النهاية" في شرح الهداية. توفّى رحمه الله تعالى سنة ٨١٥هـ.
The second case: where it is permissible to act and issue a fatwa according to another madhhab is that the mufti is deeply learned in the madhhab, knowledgeable of evidence, has deep insight into the Qur'an and Sunnah, even if he has not reached the level of ijtihad, but he comes across a sound hadith with clear indication and finds no objection to it except the statement of his imam. Then it is permissible for him to adopt the opinion of a mujtahid who acted upon that hadith, as we detailed in the chapter on taqlid and adopting a madhhab. This is in agreement with what Allamah Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) narrated in Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti from Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Bayri, from Sharh al-Hidayah by Ibn al-Shahnah al-Kabir: "If a hadith is authentic and contradicts the madhhab, act upon the hadith, and that becomes his madhhab, and his follower does not cease to be Hanafi by acting upon it." It is authentically reported from Abu Hanifa that he said: "If a hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab." And Imam Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated this from Abu Hanifa and other imams, and Imam al-Sha'rani also transmitted it from the four imams. I say: It is not hidden that this applies only to one who is qualified to examine the texts and distinguish their abrogated from their abrogating. Then he considered his name. [Footnote]: Ibn al-Shahnah al-Kabir: He is Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud Abu al-Walid Muhibb al-Din, Ibn al-Shahnah al-Kabir al-Halabi, father of Abu al-Fadl Muhammad Ibn al-Shahnah al-Saghir. The family name Ibn al-Shahnah is traced to an ancestor who was a shahnah (chief of police) of Aleppo, what we call today head of police or director of police. (Margin note on al-A'lam 7:51) A Hanafi jurist, also engaged in literature and history, a scholar of Aleppo. He served as judge there multiple times and also in Damascus and Cairo. His works include: Rawd al-Manazir fi Ilm al-Awa'il wa al-Awakhir, an abridgment of Abu al-Fida's history with additions up to 806 AH, a book on the Prophet's biography, a poem and its commentary, and Nihayat al-Nihaya fi Sharh al-Hidayah. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in 815 AH.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage outlines the second scenario where a mufti may issue a fatwa according to a madhhab other than his own: when he discovers a sound hadith with clear evidence that contradicts his imam's opinion. The mufti must be deeply versed in his madhhab, knowledgeable of evidence, and capable of critical textual analysis—even if not a full mujtahid. He encounters an authentic hadith whose meaning is clear, with no conflicting evidence except the opinion of his own imam. In such a case, he may adopt the view of a mujtahid who followed that hadith. The author confirms that this is consistent with the famous statement of Imam Abu Hanifa: 'If a hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab.' This principle is transmitted by Ibn Abd al-Barr and al-Sha'rani from the four imams. Importantly, the author adds that this applies only to those qualified to examine texts and distinguish abrogated from abrogating rulings. The biographical note on Ibn al-Shahnah al-Kabir provides context about a Hanafi scholar who transmitted this ruling. The passage emphasizes that acting on the sahih hadith does not remove the follower from the Hanafi madhhab; rather, it remains their school because the mufti is following the essence of the founder's methodology.

Key Terms
متبحر (mutabahhir): A deeply learned scholar in the madhhab, thoroughly knowledgeable of its evidence and methodology.
حديث صحيح (hadith sahih): A hadith with an uninterrupted chain of reliable narrators, free from irregularity and hidden defect, and with clear legal indication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must a mufti meet to act on a hadith contrary to his madhhab?
A) He must be a mujtahid mutlaq.
B) He must be deeply learned in the madhhab, knowledgeable of evidence, and able to distinguish abrogated from abrogating.
C) He must have received permission from the four imams.
D) He must only act on hadith that are mutawatir.

Key Takeaway
A qualified Hanafi mufti may issue a fatwa based on a sahih hadith even if it contradicts the madhhab, provided he is mutabahhir and capable of textual analysis.

Overturning a Judge's Ruling in Ijtihad Matters
Analyzing when a second judge may overturn the first judge's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a judicial ruling according to the four scenarios from al-Kasani and identify whether a second judge may overturn it in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A ruling on a matter unanimously agreed as ijtihad is final; a ruling in a disputed matter may be overturned if the ruling itself is disputed.

This passage from al-Kasani, as cited by Muhammad Taqi Usmani, lays out the Hanafi principles governing when a second judge can overturn the first judge's ruling. It is essential for muftis and judges to understand these classifications to maintain consistency and finality in Islamic judiciary. We will parse the four scenarios and the intra-Hanafi disagreement on later consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main axes
Distinguish between (1) the ruling itself being subject to ijtihad (e.g., its validity is disputed) and (2) the object of the ruling being subject to ijtihad (but the validity of the ruling is agreed).
The first axis concerns rulings like confinement of a free man; the second concerns matters like the sale of an umm walad.
2
Determine consensus on the matter as a valid subject of ijtihad
Check if there is agreement that the matter is a place of ijtihad. If agreed (mujma' 'alayh), the ruling stands; if not agreed (mukhtalaf fih), further analysis is needed.
The 'shocking ijtihad' distinction is critiqued—once a matter is ijtihad, all opinions are equally valid.
3
Apply al-Kasani's four scenarios
Use the summary: (1) ruling on a matter of consensus: must agree with it; (2) object agreed to be ijtihad: ruling stands by agreement; (3) object disputed as ijtihad: ruling stands per Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf but not per Muhammad; (4) ruling itself disputed: does not stand per those who consider it invalid.
This is the core analytic framework for a mufti.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on later consensus
Note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that later consensus (ijma' muta'akhkhir) does not remove earlier disagreement, so a first ruling remains valid. Muhammad holds that it does remove it, so a ruling against later consensus is void.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in the umm walad case, the ruling stands or is overturned based on which view the second judge follows.
5
Critically assess the 'shocking ijtihad' view
Some later Hanafis allowed overturning if the ijtihad is 'shocking.' The author questions this because if it is genuine ijtihad, there is no basis to distinguish.
This shows the methodological rigor required in mufti adab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان نفس القضاء مجتهداً فيه أنه يجوز أم لا؟ كما لو قضى بالحَجْرِ على الحُرّ، أو قضى على الغائب، إنّه يجوز للقاضى الثانى أن ينقض قضاء الأول إذا مال اجتهاده إلى خلاف اجتهاد الأول، لأن قضاءه هنا لم يجز بقول الكُل، بل بقولِ البعض دون البعض، فلم يكن جوازه متفقاً عليه، فكان محتملاً للنقض بمثله، بخلاف الفصل الأول، لأن جواز القضاء هناك ثبت بقول الكل، فكان متفقاً عليه، فلا يَحْتَمِلُ النّقض بقول البعض. ولأن المسألة إذا كانت مختلفاً فيها، فالقاضى بالقضاء يقطع أحد الاختلافين، ويجعله متفقاً عليه في الحكم بالقضاء المتفق على جوازه، وإذا كان نفس القضاء مختلفاً فيه، يرفع الخلاف بالخلاف"
"هذا إذا كان القضاء فى محل أجمعوا على كونه محل الاجتهاد. فأما إذا كان في محل اختلفوا أنه محل الاجتهاد أم لا؟ كبيع أم الولد، هل ينفذ قضاء القاضى أم لا؟ فعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله ينفذ، لأنه محل الاجتهاد عندهما لاختلاف الصحابة في جواز بيعها، وعند محمد لا ينفذ لوقوع الاتفاق بعد ذلك من الصحابة وغيرهم على أنه لا يجوز بيعها، فخرج عن محل الاجتهاد. وهذا يرجع إلى أن الإجماع المتأخر هل يرفع الخلاف المتقدم؟ عندهما لا يرفع وعنده يرفع فكان هذا الفصل مختلفاً في كونه مجتهداً فيه، فيُنظر إن كان من رأي القاضى الثانى أنه يجتهد فيه، ينفذ قضاؤه، ولا يرده لما ذكرنا في سائر المجتهدات المتفق عليها، وإن كان من رأيه أنه خرج عن حد الاجتهاد، وصار متفقاً عليه لا ينفذ، بل يرده لأن عنده أن قضاء الأول وقع مخالفاً للإجماع، فكان باطلاً.
ومن مشايخنا من فصل فى المجتهدات تفصيلاً آخر، فقال: إن كان الاجتهاد شنيعاً مستنكراً، جاز للقاضى الثانى أن ينقض قضاء الأول. وهذا فيه نظر، لأنه إذا صح كونه محل الاجتهاد، فلا معنى للفصل بين مجتهد ومجتهد، لأن ما ذكرنا من المعنى لا يوجب الفصل بينهما، فينبغي أن لا يجوز للثاني نقض قضاء الأول، لأن قضاءه صادف محل الاجتهاد. (1)
وحاصل ماذكره الكاساني رحمه الله تعالى ما يأتي:
إن كان القضاء فى مسئلةٍ مُجْمَعِ عليها، فما وافق الإجماع نفذ، وما خالفه بطل.
إن كان المقضى به مجتهداً فيه، ولا خلاف في كونه مجتهداً فيه، نفذ القضاء بالاتفاق.
إن كان هناك خلاف فى كون المقضى به مجتهداً فيه، نفذ القضاء عند أبي حنيفة وأبى يوسف، ولم ينفذ عند محمد رحمهم الله تعالى. إن كان القضاء نفسه مجتهداً فيه، مثل القضاء على الغائب، والحجر على الحر، لم ينفذ القضاء عند من لا يجوزه وإن الأولى والثانية من هذه النقاط الأربع لا يحتاجان إلى شرح وتفصيل، كما هو ظاهر.
(1) المراد أنّ كونه قضاء معتبراً فيه خلاف والقضاء الذى ينفذ في المجتهدات إنما هو القضاء الذي ثبت كونه قضاء بالاتفاق.
(1) بدائع الصنائع كتاب أدب القاضي، فصل: ما ينفذ من القضايا وما لا ينفذ ٥ : ٤٥٧ ، ٤٥٨
And if the ruling itself is subject to ijtihad (whether it is permissible or not?), such as if he ruled for confinement of a free man, or ruled against an absentee: it is permissible for the second judge to overturn the first judge's ruling if his ijtihad inclines contrary to the first judge's ijtihad, because here his ruling was not permitted by the consensus of all, but rather by the opinion of some and not others, so its permissibility was not unanimously agreed upon, and thus it is possible to be overturned by something similar. Unlike the first instance, because there the permissibility of the ruling was established by the consensus of all, so it was unanimously agreed upon, and it does not admit overturning by the opinion of some. And because if the matter is disputed, the judge (by his ruling) cuts one of the two differences and makes it unanimous in a ruling whose permissibility is agreed upon; but if the ruling itself is disputed, he removes disagreement with disagreement.
This is when the ruling concerns a matter they have agreed is a place of ijtihad. But if it concerns a matter they have disputed whether it is a place of ijtihad or not — like the sale of the umm walad, does the judge's ruling take effect or not? According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them), it takes effect, because it is a place of ijtihad in their view due to the disagreement of the Companions on the permissibility of selling her; according to Muhammad, it does not take effect because later agreement occurred by the Companions and others that selling her is not permissible, so it fell out of the place of ijtihad. This turns on whether later consensus (ijma' muta'akhkhir) removes earlier disagreement? In their view it does not remove; in his view it does remove. So this chapter differs on whether it is subject to ijtihad: if the second judge's opinion is that it is subject to ijtihad, his ruling takes effect and he does not reject it for what we mentioned regarding other agreed ijtihad matters; if his opinion is that it has left the limit of ijtihad and become agreed upon, it does not take effect, rather he rejects it, because in his view the first judge's ruling contradicted consensus, so it was void.
Some of our scholars have made another detailed distinction about ijtihad matters, saying: if the ijtihad is shocking and objectionable, it is permissible for the second judge to overturn the first judge's ruling. But this is questionable, because if it is established as a place of ijtihad, there is no meaning to distinguishing between one ijtihad and another, because the meaning we mentioned does not necessitate a distinction between them; so it is not permissible for the second to overturn the first's ruling, because his ruling encountered a place of ijtihad. (1)
The summary of what al-Kasani (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned is as follows:
If the ruling concerns a matter unanimously agreed upon, then what agrees with consensus takes effect, and what contradicts it is void.
If the object of the ruling is subject to ijtihad and there is no disagreement that it is subject to ijtihad, the ruling takes effect by agreement.
If there is disagreement about whether the object of the ruling is subject to ijtihad, the ruling takes effect according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and does not take effect according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them).
If the ruling itself is subject to ijtihad, like ruling against an absentee and confinement of a free man, the ruling does not take effect according to those who do not permit it.
And the first and second of these four points do not need explanation and detail, as is apparent.
(1) The intended meaning is that its being a considered ruling is disputed, and the ruling that takes effect in ijtihad matters is only the ruling whose status as a ruling is established by consensus.
(1) Bada'i' al-Sana'i', Book of Adab al-Qadi, Chapter: What takes effect of rulings and what does not, 5:457-458.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
The passage discusses the principles governing whether a second judge can overturn the first judge's ruling. It is a crucial issue in mufti adab and judicial practice. The text opens by distinguishing two scenarios: (1) when the ruling itself is subject to ijtihad (i.e., whether such a ruling is legally valid at all), and (2) when the matter being ruled upon is subject to ijtihad but the validity of the ruling is agreed. In the first scenario, if the ruling itself is controversial (like confinement of a free man or judgment against an absentee), a second judge may overturn it if his ijtihad differs, because the permissibility of such a ruling was not unanimously agreed. The author provides the ratio: when the ruling's validity is disputed, overturning it replaces one difference with another, which is acceptable. In contrast, if the ruling is on a matter of ijtihad but the validity of the ruling was agreed by all (like a ruling in a matter unanimously considered ijtihad), it cannot be overturned because it was based on consensus.

The text then addresses a complication: what if the matter itself is disputed as to whether it is a valid subject of ijtihad? The example given is the sale of an umm walad (a slave mother who has borne her master's child). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, this is a matter of ijtihad, so the first judge's ruling (whether for or against sale) is valid and cannot be overturned. According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, later consensus (ijma' muta'akhkhir) among the Companions established that selling her is not permissible; thus the issue is no longer a matter of ijtihad, and a ruling to sell her would be invalid and can be overturned. This disagreement between the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad hinges on whether later consensus removes earlier disagreement. The ruling of the second judge depends on his own view of the matter: if he believes it is still a matter of ijtihad, he lets the first ruling stand; if he believes it is settled, he overturns it.

The text then mentions a view from some later Hanafi scholars who distinguish between 'shocking' ijtihad (ijtihad shani' mustankar) and acceptable ijtihad, allowing overturning only in shocking cases. The author criticizes this view, reasoning that once a matter is genuinely a subject of ijtihad, all ijtihad positions are equally valid, so no distinction should be made.

Finally, the passage summarizes four points from Imam al-Kasani: (1) If the ruling is on a matter of consensus, it is valid only if it agrees with consensus. (2) If the object of the ruling is agreed to be ijtihad, the ruling stands by agreement. (3) If there is disagreement on whether it is ijtihad, the ruling stands according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf but not according to Muhammad. (4) If the ruling itself (its validity) is disputed, it does not stand according to those who consider it invalid.

Key Terms
محل الاجتهاد (mahall al-ijtihad): A matter that is open to independent legal reasoning because there is no definitive text (nass) or consensus (ijma') on it.
الإجماع المتأخر (al-ijma' al-muta'akhkhir): A consensus that occurs at a later time, after an earlier disagreement on a legal issue.
نقض القضاء (naqd al-qada'): The act of a second judge overturning or annulling a ruling issued by a previous judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the four-point summary from al-Kasani, what is the rule for a ruling whose object is subject to ijtihad AND there is no disagreement that it is a subject of ijtihad?
A) The ruling takes effect by agreement and cannot be overturned.
B) The ruling takes effect only if it agrees with the second judge's ijtihad.
C) The ruling does not take effect because it is subject to ijtihad.
D) The ruling is void and can be overturned unconditionally.

Key Takeaway
A second judge may only overturn a first judge's ruling if the ruling itself is disputed (its validity not agreed upon), not if the object of the ruling is agreed to be ijtihad.
