The Nine Disliked Questions for a Mufti
List of nine disliked question types for a mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and categorize the nine situations in which a mufti should avoid answering, and apply the principle that the prohibition varies in severity.

Core Idea
A mufti is not obligated to answer every question; some questions are disliked, prohibited, or require special conditions.

This lesson presents nine categories of questions that a mufti should handle with caution or avoid altogether. These guidelines, drawn from Ibn al-Salah and al-Shatibi, protect the integrity of fatwa and prevent misuse. Understanding them equips you to exercise proper discretion as a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Read the nine points
Carefully read the list of nine situations where questioning is disliked. Note the sequence from point four to nine (the text skips the first three points which are covered earlier).
The text begins with 'الرابع' (Fourth) – points 1-3 are not included in this excerpt.
2
Identify the core concern of each point
For each of the nine cases, ask: What is the underlying reason that makes this question disliked? (e.g., hypothetical, dependent on custom, contentious, etc.)
Use the key terms provided to help categorize the motives.
3
Classify the severity level
Al-Shatibi notes that the prohibition is not uniform: some cases are severely disliked, some light, some prohibited, and some subject to ijtihad. Assign a probable severity to each point based on the wording (e.g., 'no permissible' for point five, 'prohibition of aghlutat' for point six).
Look for clues like 'لا يجوز' (not permissible) vs. 'يكره' (disliked).
4
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Imagine a mufti is asked a question from each category. Decide whether he should answer, redirect, or refuse, and justify using the passage.
Focus on the mufti's discretion and ethical responsibility.
5
Summarize the guiding principle
Articulate the overarching maxim: The mufti must consider the context, the questioner's intention, and his own knowledge before answering.
This reflects the adab al-mufti tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: روى عن بعض الفقهاء أنهم منعوا المفتى من أن يُفتى للناس في مسائل لم تقع لهم. وقد ذكرنا فى أوّل الكتاب أقوال السلف الذين كانوا يكرهون أن يتكلموا فى المسائل التى لم تقع بعد، واختلاف وجهات النظر في ذلك. وذكرنا هناك أنّ الإجابة على مثل هذه الأسئلة ينبغي أن تقتصر على من يُريدُ التّفقة من طلبة العلم. أمّا عامة الناس، فلا ينبغي أن يُشجعوا على مثل هذه الأسئلة. الخامس: إذا كانَ حُكمُ المسئلةِ مبنيًّا على عرف خاص ببلد أو قوم، ولا يعرف المفتى عُرف ذلك البلد أو القوم. قال ابن الصلاح رحمه الله تعالى: "لا يجوز له أن يُفتى فى الأيمان والأقارير ونحو ذلك مما يتعلق بالألفاظ، إلاّ إذا كان من أهل بلد اللافظ بها، أو منزلاً منزلتهم في الخبرةِ بمراداتهم من ألفاظهم وتعارفهم فيها، لأنه إذا لم يكن كذلك، كثر خطاه عليهم في ذلك، كما شهدت به التجربة." السادس: ذكر الإمام الشاطبي رحمه الله تعالى من جملة ما يُكره فيها السؤال: أن يُسأل عن صعاب المسائل وشرارها، كما جاء في النّهى عن الأغلوطات. السابع: أن يُسأل عن علة الحكم، وهو من قبيل التعبدات التي لا يُعقل لها معنى، مثل أن يسأل: لماذا كانت ركعات المغرب ثلاثة؟ الثامن: ذكر الإمام الشاطبي رحمه الله تعالى من جملة هذه المواضع السؤال عمّا شَجَرَ بين السلف الصالح. وقد سُئل عمر بن عبد العزيز رحمه الله تعالى عن قتال أهل صفين، فقال: تلك دماء كف الله عنها يدى، فلا أُحبُّ أن يَلْطَحَ بها لسانی. التاسع: وذكر رحمه الله من جملتها سؤال التعنت والإفحام وطلب الغلبة في الخصام. وفي القرآن في ذمّ نحو هذا وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يُعْجِبُكَ قَوْلُهُ فِي الْحَيَوةِ الدُّنْيَا وَيُشْهِدُ اللهَ عَلَى مَا فِي قَلْبِهِ وَهُوَ أَلَهُ الْخِصَامِ [البقرة : ٢٠٤] وقال: بَل هُمْ قَوْمُ خَصِمُونَ [الزخرف : ٥٨] وفى الحديث: أبْغَضَ الرِّجَالِ إلى اللهِ الأَلَد الخصم. ثمّ قال الشاطبي رحمه الله تعالى: "هذه جملة من المواضع التي يُكره السؤال فيها، ويُقاس عليه ما سواها. وليس النّهى فيها واحداً، بل فيها ما تشتد كَرَاهِيتُه، ومنها ما يخف، ومنها ما يحرم ، ومنها ما يكون محل اجتهاد."
Fourth: It is narrated from some jurists that they prevented the mufti from issuing fatwas to people about matters that have not occurred for them. We have mentioned at the beginning of the book the statements of the predecessors who disliked speaking about matters that have not yet occurred, and the differing viewpoints on that. We mentioned there that answering such questions should be limited to those who desire understanding from students of knowledge. As for the general public, they should not be encouraged to ask such questions. Fifth: If the ruling of an issue is based on a specific custom of a country or people, and the mufti does not know the custom of that country or people. Ibn al-Salah said: 'It is not permissible for him to issue fatwas regarding oaths, acknowledgments, and the like that pertain to words, unless he is from the people of the country of the speaker, or placed in their position in knowledge of their intended meanings from their words and their conventions in them, because if he is not, his errors regarding them are many, as experience has shown.' Sixth: Imam al-Shatibi mentioned among the matters in which questioning is disliked: that one be asked about difficult and problematic questions, as in the prohibition of 'aghlutat.' Seventh: That one be asked about the cause of a ruling, which is of the category of devotional acts that have no intelligible meaning, such as asking: Why are the rak'ahs of Maghrib three? Eighth: Imam al-Shatibi mentioned among these topics the question about what occurred among the righteous predecessors. Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz was asked about the fighting of the people of Siffin, so he said: 'That is blood from which Allah restrained my hand, so I would not love that my tongue gets stained with it.' Ninth: He mentioned among them the question of obstinacy, silencing, and seeking dominance in argument. In the Quran, in condemnation of this: 'And of the people is he whose speech pleases you in worldly life, and he calls Allah to witness over what is in his heart, yet he is the most contentious of opponents' [al-Baqarah 2:204] and He said: 'But they are a contentious people' [al-Zukhruf 43:58]. In the hadith: 'The most hateful men to Allah is the most contentious opponent.' Then al-Shatibi said: 'This is a collection of topics in which questioning is disliked, and what is similar to them is analogized to them. The prohibition is not uniform; rather, some are severely disliked, some are light, some are prohibited, and some are subject to ijtihad.'
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a list of nine situations in which a mufti should avoid or be cautious in answering questions, based on the works of Ibn al-Salah and al-Shatibi. The author, Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani, presents these as ethical guidelines for the mufti. The fourth point warns against answering hypothetical questions for the general public, as this was the practice of the early Muslims; such questions may only be appropriate for students seeking legal understanding. The fifth point emphasizes the importance of being familiar with the local custom ('urf) when issuing fatwas on matters that depend on it, especially regarding oaths and acknowledgments; ignorance of the custom can lead to error. The sixth and seventh points advise against difficult questions that are meant to test or trip up the mufti (aghlutat), and against asking for the rationale behind purely devotional acts (ta'abbudat) like the number of rak'ahs in Maghrib. The eighth point discourages revisiting historical disputes among the Companions, as illustrated by the response of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz regarding the Battle of Siffin. The ninth point condemns questions asked out of obstinacy, to silence the mufti, or to win an argument, citing Quranic verses and a hadith about the contentious opponent. Finally, al-Shatibi explains that the degree of prohibition varies: some are severely disliked, some mild, some outright haram, and some subject to ijtihad. This demonstrates that the mufti is not obligated to answer every question; he must exercise discretion and adhere to proper adab.

Key Terms
الأغلوطات (al-aghluṭāt): Difficult or tricky questions meant to confuse the mufti or lead him into error.
التعنت (al-taʿannut): Obstinacy or willful persistence in asking questions in a hostile manner.
الإفحام (al-ifḥām): Attempting to silence the mufti by asking a question that supposedly has no answer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on asking a mufti about the cause (ʿillah) of a purely devotional act (taʿabbud), such as the number of rakʿahs in Maghrib?
A) It is obligatory to answer because every ruling has a cause.
B) It is permissible and encouraged to seek understanding.
C) It is disliked (makruh) because such matters are not rationally explicable.
D) It is prohibited (haram) without exception.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must exercise discretion in answering questions, avoiding those that are hypothetical, custom-dependent, tricky, devotional, historical, or argumentative, as these are disliked or prohibited.

Obligation to Retract a Wrong Fatwa
Ruling on retraction with a precedent from Umar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mufti must retract an erroneous fatwa and apply Umar's directive to a real scenario.

Core Idea
A mufti must retract an erroneous fatwa; persistence in error is forbidden.

A mufti's duty is to convey Allah's ruling, not to defend his own ego. When an error becomes apparent, the obligation to correct it is clear. The source presents this fundamental adab with a powerful precedent from Caliph Umar, making the ruling both principled and practical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Find the explicit statement: 'it is obligatory upon the mufti... to retract his previous fatwa'. Note the word 'wajib' (obligatory).
The ruling is wajib, not just recommended.
2
Locate the Evidence
The author cites a letter from Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Identify the key phrases: 'Do not let a judgment... prevent you from returning to the truth'.
This is a dalil naqli from the practice of a Companion, which in Hanafi usul is a source (qawl sahabi).
3
Understand the Rationale
Umar's statement explains why: 'the truth is pre-eternal, and nothing nullifies it. Returning to the truth is better than persisting in falsehood.' The rationale is that truth is timeless and superior to personal consistency.
The mufti's duty is to the truth, not to his previous opinion.
4
Apply to a Scenario
Imagine a mufti issued a fatwa permitting a sale, then learns it involved hidden interest. He must retract the fatwa and inform the questioner, even if it causes some embarrassment.
This application shows the ruling in action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرجوع عن الفتوى
يَجب على المُفتى إن ظَهَرَ خطأ فى فتواه أن يرجع عن فتواه السابقة، وأن لا يَخْجَل من ذلك. وجاء فى خطاب سيدنا عمر بن الخطاب إلى أبي موسى الأشعري رضى الله تعالى عنهما: "لا يَمْنَعنك قضاء قضيته بالأمس راجعت فيه نفسك وهديت لرشدك أن تُراجع الحق، فإن الحق قديم، وإن الحق لا يبطله شيء، ومُراجعة الحَقِّ خير من التمادى فى الباطل."
Retraction of the Fatwa. It is obligatory upon the mufti, if an error appears in his fatwa, to retract his previous fatwa, and not to be ashamed of that. And it is narrated in the letter of our master Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Do not let a judgment you passed yesterday, upon which you reflected and were guided to the right course, prevent you from returning to the truth, for the truth is pre-eternal, and nothing nullifies the truth. Returning to the truth is better than persisting in falsehood.'
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental rule of mufti conduct: if a mufti realizes he made a mistake, he must retract the fatwa and not be too ashamed to do so. The obligation (wujub) of retraction is clear. The author supports this with the famous directive of Caliph Umar to his judge Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, which emphasizes that returning to the truth is mandatory and that past decisions do not bind one to error. The phrase 'the truth is pre-eternal (qadim)' means truth is timeless and not subject to personal pride. This principle ensures that muftis prioritize correctness over ego, and it protects the public from following erroneous rulings.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الفتوى (al-rujūʿ ʿan al-fatwā): The act of retracting or withdrawing a previously given fatwa upon realizing it was incorrect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the obligation on a mufti if an error becomes apparent in his fatwa?
A) He may remain silent and hope it is overlooked.
B) He must retract the fatwa and not be ashamed.
C) He should refer the question to another mufti.
D) He should maintain his original ruling to avoid confusion.

Key Takeaway
Retracting a wrong fatwa is a divine obligation, not a sign of weakness; truth is timeless and must be prioritized over personal pride.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti

Retraction of a Fatwa: When Past Actions Must Be Undone
Ruling on when a mufti must retract and how previous actions are affected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on retraction of a fatwa by distinguishing between cases that require nullification of past actions and those that do not.

Core Idea
Retracting an erroneous fatwa is obligatory; past actions stand if the error was in an ijtihad matter.

A mufti is human and may err. When he realizes his fatwa was wrong, Islamic ethics demand immediate retraction without shame. But does that mean everyone who relied on the fatwa must undo their actions? The answer depends on the nature of the evidence: if the fatwa contradicted a decisive text (qati'), the action is void; if it was a matter of ijtihad, the principle 'ijtihad does not nullify ijtihad' protects past validity. This lesson unpacks this crucial distinction through classical evidence and the story of Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mufti's Duty
Recognize that a mufti must retract his fatwa if he discovers an error, as per Umar's directive to Abu Musa. The duty is obligatory (wajib) when the error is certain.
Umar's letter emphasizes returning to truth over persisting in falsehood.
2
Distinguish Two Scenarios of Action
If the questioner has not yet acted on the fatwa, he must abandon it. If he has acted, we examine the type of evidence the fatwa contradicted.
Al-Nawawi's text is the basis.
3
Apply the Qati' vs. Ijtihad Test
If the retracted fatwa contradicted a decisive evidence (dalil qati'), the past action must be nullified (e.g., divorce). If it was a matter open to ijtihad, the action stands because 'ijtihad does not nullify ijtihad'.
This is the core legal principle.
4
Analyze the Ibn Mas'ud Incident
Ibn Mas'ud initially permitted a man to marry his wife's mother based on his ijtihad. After learning the correct prohibition (qati' dalil), he ordered separation. This shows nullification when the error contradicts clear text.
Al-Khatib's explanation shows the ijtihad was based on a misreading.
5
Internalize the Qawida and Its Exception
The qawida 'al-ijtihad la yanqudu al-ijtihad' applies only where ijtihad is valid. The exception is when the earlier ijtihad contradicts a qati' text, which then requires nullification.
This aligns with 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرجوع عن الفتوى
يَجب على المُفتى إن ظَهَرَ خطأ فى فتواه أن يرجع عن فتواه السابقة، وأن لا يَخْجَل من ذلك. وجاء فى خطاب سيدنا عمر بن الخطاب إلى أبي موسى الأشعري رضى الله تعالى عنهما: "لا يَمْنَعنك قضاء قضيته بالأمس راجعت فيه نفسك وهديت لرشدك أن تُراجع الحق، فإن الحق قديم، وإن الحق لا يبطله شيء، ومُراجعة الحَقِّ خير من التمادى فى الباطل."
ثم قال النووي رحمه الله تعالى: "إذا أفتى بشيئ ثم رجع عنه، ولم يكن عمِلَ بالأول، لم يجز العمل به. وإن كان عَمِلَ قبل رجوعه، فإن خالف دليلاً قاطعاً، لزم المستفتى نقض عمله ذلك، وكذا إن نكح بفتواه، واستمر على نكاح بفتواه، ثم رجع لزمه مفارقتها." ومما يدل على ذلك ماروى البيهقي وغيره أن رجلاً من بنى شَمْخ من فَزارة تزوج امرأةٌ، ثم رأى أمها فأعْجَبته، فاستفتى ابن مسعود عن ذلك، فأمره أن يُفارقها ويتزوج أمها، فتزوجها، فولدت له أولاداً، ثم أتى ابن مسعود المدينة، فسأل عن ذلك، فأخبر أنها لا تحل له، فلما رجع إلى الكوفة قال للرجل : إنّها عليك حرام، إنّها لا تنبغى لك، ففارقها . و قال الخطيب رحمه الله تعالى: "لعل ابن مسعود رضى الله تعالى عنه تأوّل فتواه قول الله تعالى: \" فَإِن لَّمْ تَكُونُوا دَخَلْتُم بِهِنَّ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ \" [النساء : ۲۳] أن الاستثناءَ راجع إلى أمهات النِّساءِ وإلى الربائب جميعاً."
ثمّ قال النووي رحمه الله تعالى: "وإن كان (أى الأمر المرجوع عنه) محل اجتهاد لم يلزمه نقضه، لأن الاجتهاد لا ينقض الاجتهاد. وهذا التفصيل ..."
Retracting a Fatwa: It is obligatory upon the mufti, if an error appears in his fatwa, to retract his previous fatwa, and not to be ashamed of that. And it came in the letter of our master Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Do not let a judgment you made yesterday, after which you reconsidered and were guided to what is right, prevent you from returning to the truth, for the truth is eternal, and nothing nullifies the truth, and returning to the truth is better than persisting in falsehood.' Then al-Nawawi said: 'If he gave a fatwa on something and then retracted it, and the first was not acted upon, it is not permissible to act upon it. But if it was acted upon before his retraction, then if it contradicts decisive evidence, the questioner must nullify that action; likewise if he married based on his fatwa and continued in that marriage, then he retracted, he must separate from her.' And among the evidence for that is what al-Bayhaqi and others narrated: that a man from Banu Shamkh of Fazara married a woman, then saw her mother and was attracted to her, so he asked Ibn Mas'ud for a fatwa, and he ordered him to divorce her and marry the mother, so he married her and she bore him children. Then Ibn Mas'ud went to Medina and asked about the matter, and he was told she is not lawful for him. When he returned to Kufa, he said to the man: 'She is haram for you, she is not permissible for you,' so he separated from her. And al-Khatib said: 'Perhaps Ibn Mas'ud based his fatwa on the interpretation of Allah's saying: "...if you have not entered into them, then there is no sin upon you..." [al-Nisa' 23] that the exception applies to both mothers of wives and step-daughters.' Then al-Nawawi said: 'If the matter (i.e., the retracted ruling) is subject to ijtihad, then he is not obliged to nullify it, because ijtihad is not nullified by ijtihad. And this detail...'
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents a methodological rule for muftis: when a mufti realizes his fatwa was erroneous, he must retract it publicly and without shame. The passage quotes Umar's letter to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari emphasizing that returning to truth is better than persisting in falsehood. Al-Nawawi then distinguishes two scenarios: if the questioner has not yet acted on the fatwa, they must abandon it; if they have acted and the fatwa contradicted definitive evidence (dalil qati'), they must undo the action (e.g., divorce if married based on the erroneous fatwa). The story of Ibn Mas'ud illustrates this: he initially permitted a man to marry his wife's mother (based on his interpretation of the verse), but later learned the prohibition was general, so he ordered the man to separate. Finally, al-Nawawi introduces an important principle: if the retracted fatwa was based on ijtihad (a matter open to interpretation), then the previous action is not nullified, because 'ijtihad does not nullify ijtihad'. This is a key qa'idah in Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الفتوى (al-ruju' 'an al-fatwa): The act of the mufti retracting his previous fatwa after realizing it was erroneous.
نقض الفتوى (naqd al-fatwa): Nullification of the legal effects of a retracted fatwa.
الاجتهاد لا ينقض الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad la yanqudu al-ijtihad): A principle that a previous ijtihad-based ruling is not overturned by a later ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Nawawi as cited in this lesson, when must a questioner nullify an action performed based on a retracted fatwa?
A) Always, if the fatwa was incorrect.
B) Only if the fatwa contradicted decisive evidence (dalil qati').
C) Only if the fatwa contradicted a previous ijtihad.
D) Never, because ijtihad does not nullify ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must retract an erroneous fatwa, but past actions are only undone if the fatwa contradicted decisive evidence; otherwise, ijtihad protects past validity.

Obligation to Inform the Mustafti of Retraction
Stating the duty of the mufti to inform the inquirer if he retracts his fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a mufti must inform the mustafti of a retraction, distinguishing cases where the mustafti has or has not acted on the fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must correct a wrong fatwa even if it means publicly searching for the asker.

A mufti's responsibility does not end with issuing a fatwa; if he later discovers an error, he must actively seek out the mustafti to correct it. This duty, derived from the Hanafi tradition, ensures that the fatwa does not lead to wrongful action. The passage cites the exemplary conduct of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, who hired a crier to find the person he had misinformed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the phrase that states the obligation: 'وَيَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُفْتِي أَنْ يُخْبِرَ الْمُسْتَفْتِي عَنْ رُجُوعِهِ'. This is a wajib (obligatory) duty.
The ruling applies whether or not the mustafti has acted.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Note the two cases: (1) the mustafti has not acted – simply inform; (2) the mustafti has acted and the act is invalid – inform so he can annul it.
The detail is referenced but not elaborated here; focus on the existence of the duty.
3
Analyze the historical example
Read the story of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. He hired a crier and stopped issuing fatwas until he found the asker. This shows the lengths a mufti must go to correct an error.
The example serves as a binding precedent (dalil naqli) for the ruling.
4
Derive the operative principle
The principle is: a mufti's obligation to correct errors overrides personal inconvenience or reputation. The mustafti's right to correct information is paramount.
This is a key adab (etiquette) for muftis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الإفتاء ومنهجه إعلام المستفتى بالرجوع عن الفتوى ويجب على المفتى أن يُخبر المستفتى عن رجوعه إن لم يَعْمَل بفتواه وكذلك إن عمل به ووجب النقض حسب التفصيل الذي ذكرناه. وقد أخرج الخطيب رحمه الله تعالى أنّ الحسن بن زياد اللُّؤْلُؤي رحمه الله تعالى أستفتى فى مسئلةٍ فأخطأ، فلم يعرف الذي أفتاه فاكترى منادياً يُنادى أن الحسن بن زياد استفتي يوم كذا وكذا فى مسئلةٍ فأخطأ، فمن كان أفتاه الحسن بن زيادٍ بشيئ فليرجع إليه. فمكث أياماً لايُفتى، حتى وجد صاحب الفتوى، فأعلمه أنه قد أخطأ، وأنّ الصواب كذا وكذا . (1)11
Rulings of Ifta' and its Methodology. Informing the Mustafti of Retraction of Fatwa. It is obligatory upon the mufti to inform the mustafti of his retraction if the mustafti has not acted on his fatwa, and likewise if he has acted on it and annulment [of the act] is required, according to the detail we have mentioned. And al-Khatib (may Allah have mercy on him) narrated that al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i (may Allah have mercy on him) was asked for a fatwa in a matter and he erred. Then he did not know the one he had given the fatwa to, so he hired a crier to announce: 'Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad was asked for a fatwa on such-and-such day in a matter and he erred. So whoever al-Hasan ibn Ziyad gave a fatwa to about something, let him return to him.' He stayed for days not giving fatwas until he found the seeker of the fatwa, and informed him that he had erred and that the correct [ruling] is such-and-such. (1) 11
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage presents a rule of mufti adab: if a mufti realizes he has given an erroneous fatwa, he must inform the mustafti. If the mustafti has not yet acted, the mufti simply informs him of the correct ruling. If the mustafti has acted and the action is invalid, the mufti must inform him so that he can rectify. The author supports this with a historical example of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i, a prominent Hanafi scholar, who publicly announced his mistake and sought out the person he had misinformed. This underscores the mufti's responsibility and the importance of preserving the integrity of the fatwa.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الفتوى (al-rujūʿ ʿan al-fatwā): The mufti's withdrawal or correction of his previously issued fatwa after realizing it was erroneous.
المستفتى (al-mustaftī): The person who seeks a fatwa from the mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Hasan ibn Ziyad do when he realized he had given an incorrect fatwa and did not know the mustafti?
A) He ignored it and continued issuing fatwas.
B) He hired a crier to announce his mistake and sought the mustafti.
C) He stopped giving fatwas permanently.
D) He asked other scholars to correct the error.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must inform the mustafti of a retraction, even if it requires public announcement and personal inconvenience.

Ruling on Taking Fees for Fatwa and the Hila of Abu Hatim al-Qazwini
Examining the permissibility of mufti fees and the hila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Abu Hatim al-Qazwini's hila to determine the permissibility of a mufti receiving payment and identify the condition that the fee must not exceed the market rate.

Core Idea
Fatwa is free; writing may be paid – but not above market rate.

The mufti is expected to serve the community without charging for his religious expertise. However, practical needs require a balance. This lesson explores the Hanafi position that a mufti may not take a fee for his oral fatwa, yet may charge for the act of writing – as a permissible legal stratagem (hila). We will dissect the conditions of this hila and understand the ethical boundaries set by the scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The passage begins by stating that a mufti is obligated not to ask for a fee for his fatwa. Recognize that the oral delivery of the fatwa is an act of religious guidance that should be free.
2
Distinguish the oral fee and the writing fee
Ibn 'Abidin clarifies that taking a fee for the oral fatwa is impermissible, but taking a fee for writing is permissible. Abstaining from even the writing fee is better. Capture the distinction: the oral act is sacred and uncompensated; the writing is a manual service that can be compensated.
3
Understand the hila (legal stratagem)
Abu Hatim al-Qazwini's stratagem: the mufti says, 'It is incumbent on me to give you the oral fatwa, but writing is not incumbent.' The mustafti then hires the mufti specifically for writing. This separates the free religious act from the paid scribal service.
The hila relies on the intention (niyyah) and explicit separation of services.
4
Apply the market rate condition
The writing fee must not exceed the fair market rate (ujr al-mithl). Any excess is considered a fee for the fatwa itself, which is prohibited. Identify this as a crucial condition to prevent circumvention of the prohibition.
5
Compare with al-Nawawi's position
Al-Nawawi states that the mufti ideally volunteers; he may take a stipend from the treasury, but only if not personally obligated and if he lacks means. Comparing both positions, note that the Hanafi hila provides a practical avenue for private compensation, while al-Nawawi's view restricts to public funds.
This step is evaluative – understand the broader fiqh context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأجرة على الإفتاء يجب علي المفتى أن لا يسئل على إفتاءه أجراً. وذكر العلامة علاوالدين ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى عن "شرح الوهبانية " أنه لا يجوز أخذ الأجرة على الإفتاء باللسان، ويجوز أخذ أجرة الكتابة، ومع هذا الكف عن ذلك أولى. (۲) وقال النووي رحمه الله تعالى: "المختار للتصدى للفتوى أن يتبرع بذلك، (۳) ويجوز أن يأخذ عليه رزقاً من بيت المال، إلا أن يتعين عليه ) وله كفاية فيحرم على الصحيح. ثم إن كان له رزق، لم يجز أخذ أجرة أصلاً، وإن لم يكن له رزق، فليس له أخذ أجرةٍ من أعيان من يُفتيه على الأصح كالحاكم. واحتال الشيخ أبو حاتم القزويني من أصحابنا فقال له أن يقول: يلزمني أن أفتِيَك قولاً، وأمّا كتابة الخط فلا. فإذا استأجره على كتابة الخط جاز. " لكن لا يجوز أن تتجاوز أجرة كتابة الفتوى على أجرة المثل، فإن ما زاد على أجرة المثل يكون أجرةً علي نفس الافتاء، وهو ممنوع. وجاء في الدر المختار:
Fee for Giving Fatwa. It is obligatory upon the mufti not to ask for a fee for his fatwa. Allamah 'Ala al-Din Ibn 'Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned from Sharh al-Wahbaniyyah that it is not permissible to take a fee for fatwa orally [bi al-lisan], and it is permissible to take a fee for writing, but abstaining from that is better. (2) And al-Nawawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'The chosen [position] for one who undertakes fatwa is to volunteer [do it without charge], (3) and it is permissible for him to take a stipend from the treasury [bayt al-mal], unless [giving fatwa] becomes [personally] obligatory upon him and he has sufficient means, then it is forbidden on the correct [opinion]. Then, if he has a stipend, it is not permissible for him to take any fee at all. And if he has no stipend, he may not take a fee from the individuals he gives fatwa to, on the correct [opinion], like the judge. And Shaykh Abu Hatim al-Qazwini, one of our scholars, devised a legal stratagem: he said that the mufti may say, 'It is incumbent upon me to give you the fatwa orally, but as for writing the line, no.' So if the mustafti hires him for writing the line, it is permissible. But the fee for writing the fatwa must not exceed the fair market rate [ujr al-mithl], for anything above that is a fee for the fatwa itself, which is prohibited. And it is stated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar:
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage treats the sensitive question of whether a mufti may accept payment. The general principle is that a mufti should not charge for his verbal fatwa. Ibn 'Abidin reports that taking a fee for the oral fatwa is impermissible, but a fee for writing it down is permissible, though refraining is better. Al-Nawawi's position is that the mufti ideally volunteers; he may take a salary from the public treasury if needed, but if fatwa is fard 'ayn on him and he is self-sufficient, even a treasury stipend is forbidden. He cannot charge individuals directly. However, a hila (legal stratagem) from Abu Hatim al-Qazwini allows the mufti to separate the oral fatwa (free) from writing (paid), but the writing fee must not exceed the customary rate. This shows the Hanafi school's concern for preserving the integrity of religious knowledge while accommodating practical needs.

Key Terms
الأجرة (al-ujrah): Fee or payment for services, specifically for fatwa or writing.
الحيلة (al-ḥīlah): A legal stratagem or device used to achieve a lawful result while avoiding a prohibition.
أجرة المثل (ujr al-mithl): The fair market rate for a similar service; used as a condition to prevent the hila from becoming a loophole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hatim al-Qazwini's hila, what is the essential condition for the writing fee?
A) It must be paid before the fatwa is given.
B) It must not exceed the fair market rate (ujr al-mithl).
C) The mustafti must agree to it in writing.
D) The mufti must dedicate the fee to charity.

Key Takeaway
A mufti may lawfully receive payment only for writing the fatwa, not for the oral fatwa, and must ensure the fee does not exceed the market rate.

Compensation for Fatwa: Fees, Salary, and Gifts
Fatawa rulings on compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and prohibited compensation for a mufti, apply the verbal vs. written fatwa distinction, and identify the conditions for accepting gifts and salaries.

Core Idea
A mufti must give the verbal fatwa free; compensation is allowed only for writing or as a salary from public funds.

This passage from Usul al-Ifta' clarifies the delicate balance between a mufti's duty to serve without charge and the need for livelihood. It distinguishes the obligatory verbal fatwa from the voluntary written service, permits salary from Bayt al-Mal, and warns against bribes disguised as gifts.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish verbal vs. written fatwa
Identify that the mufti is obligated to give the verbal fatwa without fee, but writing is an additional service for which compensation may be taken.
The obligation is on the verbal answer; writing is a separate act.
2
Apply the base rule: no fee for verbal fatwa
State the default: it is not permissible for a mufti to ask for a fee for the verbal fatwa. This applies even if he has no salary.
Exception: if fatwa is not personally obligatory and he has no means, some allow salary from Bayt al-Mal.
3
Recognize the exception for written fatwa
A fee for writing the fatwa is permissible, but it must not exceed the fair fee (ujrat al-mithl). Any excess is considered a fee for the fatwa itself and is prohibited.
The legal stratagem (hila) of Abu Hatim al-Qazwini is to explicitly state that writing is not obligatory and can be hired.
4
Evaluate salary and gift rulings
Salary from Bayt al-Mal or from community agreement is permissible if it enables devotion to fatwa. Gifts are generally permissible unless they are bribes intended to influence the fatwa.
Unlike a judge, a mufti's ruling is not binding, so gifts are less restricted.
5
Synthesize the overall hierarchy
Compile the rulings: verbal fatwa must be free; writing may be compensated; salary from public funds is allowed; gifts are allowed if not bribes. Refraining from compensation is always better.
The mufti should not commercialize his religious duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الإفتاء ومنهجه

وهذه الأحكام التي ذكرها النووي رحمه الله تعالى في مسائل الرجوع عن الفتوى أقرها كلها ابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى في "البحر"، غير أنه جَزَم بأنه لاضمان على المفتى فى صورة الإتلاف، فقال: "وإن أتلف بفتواه لا يَغْرَم، ولو كان أهلاً )

الأجرة على الإفتاء

يجب علي المفتى أن لا يسئل على إفتاءه أجراً. وذكر العلامة علاوالدين ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى عن "شرح الوهبانية " أنه لا يجوز أخذ الأجرة على الإفتاء باللسان، ويجوز أخذ أجرة الكتابة، ومع هذا الكف عن ذلك أولى.
(۲)

وقال النووي رحمه الله تعالى: "المختار للتصدى للفتوى أن يتبرع بذلك، ويجوز أن يأخذ عليه رزقاً من بيت المال، إلا أن يتعين عليه ) وله كفاية فيحرم على الصحيح. ثم إن كان له رزق، لم يجز أخذ أجرة أصلاً، وإن لم يكن له رزق، فليس له أخذ أجرةٍ من أعيان من يُفتيه على الأصح كالحاكم. واحتال الشيخ أبو حاتم القزويني من أصحابنا فقال له أن يقول: يلزمني أن أفتِيَك قولاً، وأمّا كتابة الخط فلا. فإذا استأجره على كتابة الخط جاز. " لكن لا يجوز أن تتجاوز أجرة كتابة الفتوى على أجرة المثل، فإن ما زاد على أجرة المثل يكون أجرةً علي نفس الافتاء، وهو ممنوع. وجاء في الدر المختار:

يستحق القاضى الأجر على كتب الوثائق قدرما يجوز لغيره، كالمفتى فإنّه يستحق أجر المثل على كتابة الفتوى، لأنّ الواجب عليه الجواب باللسان، دونَ الكتابة بالبنان. ومع ذلك الكف أولى. " والله أعلم.
(۱)

ثم قال النووي رحمه الله تعالى: " قال الصَّيْمَري والخطيب: لو اتفق أهل البلد فجعلوا له رزقاً من أموالهم على أن يتفرّغ لفتاويهم جاز. أما الهدية، فقال أبو مظفر السمعاني: له قبولها بخلاف الحاكم، فإنه يُلزم حكمه. قال أبو عمرو: ينبغى أن يحرُمَ قَبولها إن كانت رشوة على أن يُفتيه بمايُريد كما في الحاكم وسائر مالا يُقابل بعوض قال الخطيب: وعلى الإمام أن يَفْرِضَ لمن ينصب نفسه لتدريس الفقه والفتوى فى الأحكام ما يُغنيه عن الاحتراف ويكون ذلك من بيت المال. ثمّ روى بإسناده أن عمر بن الخطاب رضى الله عنه أعطى كل رجل ممّن هذه صفته مائة دينار في السنة. (۲)
And these rulings that al-Nawawi mentioned regarding matters of retracting a fatwa were all affirmed by Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr, except that he affirmed that there is no liability on the mufti in case of damage, saying: 'If he causes damage by his fatwa, he does not compensate, even if he was qualified.' The fee for fatwa: It is obligatory upon the mufti not to ask for a fee for his fatwa. And 'Alla' al-Din Ibn 'Abidin mentioned from Sharh al-Wahbaniyya that taking a fee for verbal fatwa is not permissible, but taking a fee for writing is permissible, and despite this, refraining from that is better. (2) Al-Nawawi said: 'The preferred choice for one who undertakes fatwa is to volunteer it, and it is permissible for him to take a salary from the Bayt al-Mal, unless it becomes personally obligatory upon him [if no other mufti exists] and he has sufficiency, then it is forbidden according to the correct view. Then, if he has a salary, it is not at all permissible to take a fee; and if he has no salary, then it is not permissible for him to take a fee from the individuals he gives fatwa to, on the most correct view, like the judge. And Shaykh Abu Hatim al-Qazwini among our companions devised a legal stratagem: he told him to say: "It is incumbent upon me to give you a fatwa verbally, but as for writing, no." So if he hires him for writing, it is permissible. But it is not permissible for the fee for writing a fatwa to exceed the fair fee, because whatever exceeds the fair fee would be a fee for the fatwa itself, which is prohibited. And it appears in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: The judge deserves the fee for writing documents as much as it is permissible for others, like the mufti, for indeed he deserves the fair fee for writing the fatwa, because what is obligatory upon him is the verbal answer, not the writing with the pen. Yet refraining is better. And Allah knows best. (1) Then al-Nawawi said: 'Al-Saymari and al-Khatib said: If the people of a city agree to give him a salary from their wealth so that he can devote himself to their fatwas, it is permissible. As for gifts, Abu Muzaffar al-Sam'ani said: He may accept them unlike the judge, because the judge's ruling is binding. Abu 'Amr said: It should be prohibited to accept them if it is a bribe for a fatwa that he desires, as in the case of the judge and all other things that are not compensated. Al-Khatib said: The Imam should assign for one who devotes himself to teaching fiqh and giving fatwas on rulings what suffices him from earning a livelihood, and that should be from Bayt al-Mal. Then he narrated with his chain that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab gave each man of this description one hundred dinars per year.'
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta discusses the rulings on compensation for a mufti. The author opens by noting that Ibn Nujaym affirmed most of Nawawi's rulings on retracting a fatwa, except that he held the mufti is not liable for damages caused by his fatwa. Then the main topic: the mufti must not ask for a fee for his fatwa. This is the default rule. However, a distinction is made between verbal and written fatwa: taking a fee for the verbal fatwa is impermissible, but taking a fee for writing the fatwa is permissible. Despite this permissibility, refraining is better. The reason is that the obligation upon the mufti is to answer verbally; writing is an additional service. Imam Nawawi adds that the preferred course is to volunteer, but if the mufti is appointed and has no other means, he may take a salary from the public treasury (Bayt al-Mal). This becomes forbidden if the fatwa is personally obligatory upon him (i.e., no other mufti exists) and he is already self-sufficient. If he has a salary, he cannot take any additional fee; if he has no salary, he still cannot take a fee from individuals he gives fatwa to, analogous to a judge. Then a legal stratagem (hila) by Shaykh Abu Hatim al-Qazwini: the mufti can say the verbal fatwa is obligatory and free, but writing is not, so he can charge for the writing service. However, the fee must not exceed the fair market rate for writing; any excess is considered a fee for the fatwa itself, which is prohibited. The passage also cites al-Durr al-Mukhtar on judges, extending the same rule. Finally, it discusses gifts and salary from the community. If the community pools money to give the mufti a salary so he can devote himself, it is permissible. As for gifts, the ruling depends: generally permissible, but if the gift is a bribe to influence the fatwa, it is prohibited. The passage ends with a recommendation from al-Khatib that the ruler should provide a sufficient stipend for scholars from Bayt al-Mal, citing the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Key Terms
الإفتاء باللسان (al-ifta' bi al-lisan): The act of delivering a fatwa verbally, which is obligatory upon the mufti without compensation.
كتابة الفتوى (kitabat al-fatwa): Writing down the fatwa, considered an additional service for which a fee may be taken.
الأجرة (al-ujrah): Compensation or fee; prohibited for the verbal fatwa, permissible for writing within fair limits.
الرزق من بيت المال (al-rizq min bayt al-mal): Salary from the public treasury for the mufti, which is permissible as long as it is not in exchange for a specific fatwa.
الهدية (al-hadiyyah): A gift given to the mufti; permissible if not a bribe to influence the fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a mufti accepting a fee for writing a fatwa?
A) Absolutely forbidden
B) Permissible, but only if it does not exceed the fair fee
C) Permissible without restrictions
D) Permissible only if the mufti has no salary

Key Takeaway
A mufti must give the verbal fatwa free, but may charge a fair fee for writing or accept a salary from public funds, and gifts are allowed if not bribes.

Compensation and Gifts for the Mufti
Rulings on mufti's compensation and acceptance of gifts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mufti's compensation and evaluate when a gift to the mufti becomes prohibited.

Core Idea
A mufti may accept a salary or ajr al-mithl for writing, but gifts are prohibited if they are bribes.

The mufti's role in issuing fatwas requires independence. Islamic law balances the need for the mufti's livelihood with the prohibition of bribery. This lesson clarifies the rules for compensation and gifts, distinguishing permissible support from corrupting influence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the ruling on the mufti's compensation for writing a fatwa: he deserves ajr al-mithl (equivalent compensation), but refraining is more virtuous.
The text analogizes the mufti to the judge regarding writing documents.
2
Locate the condition for a stipend
If the community agrees to give the mufti a regular stipend from their wealth to devote himself to fatwas, it is permissible.
This is quoted from al-Saymari and al-Khatib.
3
Analyze the gift ruling
Identify the two views: al-Sam'ani allows gifts to mufti (unlike judge); Abu Amr prohibits bribes intended to influence the fatwa.
The Hanafi position permits gifts unless they are conditional bribes.
4
Apply the distinction
Distinguish between permissible gifts and bribes: a gift without condition is permissible; a gift given with explicit or implicit expectation of a favorable fatwa is prohibited.
The mufti should exercise caution (الكف أولى).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يستحق القاضى الأجر على كتب الوثائق قدرما يجوز لغيره، كالمفتى فإنّه يستحق أجر المثل على كتابة الفتوى، لأنّ الواجب عليه الجواب باللسان، دونَ الكتابة بالبنان. ومع ذلك الكف أولى. " والله أعلم. (۱) ثم قال النووي رحمه الله تعالى: " قال الصَّيْمَري والخطيب: لو اتفق أهل البلد فجعلوا له رزقاً من أموالهم على أن يتفرّغ لفتاويهم جاز. أما الهدية، فقال أبو مظفر السمعاني: له قبولها بخلاف الحاكم، فإنه يُلزم حكمه. قال أبو عمرو: ينبغى أن يحرُمَ قَبولها إن كانت رشوة على أن يُفتيه بمايُريد كما في الحاكم وسائر مالا يُقابل بعوض قال الخطيب: وعلى الإمام أن يَفْرِضَ لمن ينصب نفسه لتدريس الفقه والفتوى فى الأحكام ما يُغنيه عن الاحتراف ويكون ذلك من بيت المال. ثمّ روى بإسناده أن عمر بن الخطاب رضى الله عنه أعطى كل رجل ممّن هذه صفته مائة دينار في السنة. (۲)
The judge deserves compensation for writing legal documents to the extent that is permissible for others, likewise the mufti deserves compensation equivalent to his work for writing the fatwa, because his obligation is to answer verbally, not in writing. Nevertheless, refraining is more virtuous. And Allah knows best. (1) Then al-Nawawi said: al-Saymari and al-Khatib said: If the people of a town agree and assign him a stipend from their wealth to devote himself to their fatwas, it is permissible. As for gifts, Abu Muzaffar al-Sam'ani said: He may accept them, unlike the judge, because his judgment is binding. Abu Amr said: It should be prohibited to accept if it is a bribe to give a fatwa according to what he wants, as in the case of the judge and everything that is not exchanged for compensation. Al-Khatib said: The imam should assign for one who dedicates himself to teaching fiqh and issuing fatwas regarding rulings what suffices him from earning, and that should be from the treasury. Then he narrated with his chain that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab gave each person of this description one hundred dinars per year. (2)
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule regarding the compensation and gifts for a mufti. The text begins by stating that the judge deserves compensation for writing documents, and analogously, the mufti deserves compensation equal to his work (ajr al-mithl) for writing a fatwa, because his obligation is to answer verbally, not in writing. However, refraining from taking payment is more virtuous. Then the text quotes al-Nawawi, who reports from al-Saymari and al-Khatib that if the community agrees to give the mufti a regular stipend (rizq) from their wealth so that he can devote himself to issuing fatwas, it is permissible. Regarding gifts (hadiyya), Abu Muzaffar al-Sam'ani says the mufti may accept them, unlike the judge who cannot because his judgment is binding. But Abu Amr says accepting gifts should be prohibited if they are a bribe to influence the fatwa. Al-Khatib recommends that the imam provide a sufficient stipend from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) for those who teach fiqh and issue fatwas, and he cites the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab giving such individuals 100 dinars annually.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): Compensation equivalent to the work performed, not a fixed fee.
الهدية (al-hadiyya): A gift given voluntarily, not part of a fee arrangement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prohibited
B) Permissible
C) Recommended but not permissible
D) Only if he has no other income

Key Takeaway
The mufti may accept compensation for writing a fatwa and a regular stipend, but gifts are prohibited if they are bribes intended to influence the fatwa.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate

The Mufti's Duty to Clarify the Question
Explains the mufti's duty to investigate and clarify the real facts behind a question

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of tanqih al-su'al to a real istifta' by identifying effective facts, posing clarifying questions, and adjusting the fatwa accordingly.

Core Idea
A fatwa is only as sound as the facts it is based on; the mufti must probe to uncover the truth.

A mufti receives a question about divorce. The questioner describes a heated argument but omits the exact words spoken. Should the mufti answer based on the written question alone? No—this lesson explains why the mufti must actively investigate and clarify the facts before issuing a fatwa. This practice, called tanqih al-su'al, protects the integrity of the fatwa and prevents it from being based on incomplete or misleading information.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the problem of incomplete questions
Understand that questioners often omit crucial legal details (effective facts) while including irrelevant ones (incidental facts). For example, in divorce cases, they describe the conflict but not the exact divorce formula.
This is common among laypeople who do not know what is legally relevant.
2
Distinguish effective facts from incidental facts
Identify which facts in the question have legal effect (waqi'at mu'aththira) and which are extraneous. The mufti must focus on the former.
Effective facts are those on which the ruling depends.
3
Apply tanqih by asking clarifying questions
The mufti should write clarifying questions on the same paper or request oral clarification. He should then base his fatwa on the clarified picture.
If oral details are added, the mufti should note them in the fatwa.
4
Learn from historical examples of failure to tanqih
Review cases like Muhammad Abduh's insurance fatwa, where a misrepresented transaction led to a fatwa being exploited. This shows the danger of not verifying real-world practices.
Imam Muhammad's practice of visiting dyers exemplifies proactive verification.
5
Implement the duty to understand real-world practices
When dealing with contemporary transactions or government laws, the mufti must study the actual practice, not just the questioner's description.
This may require reviewing legal documents or observing market practices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحكم يتعلّق به، فكأنّه لم يذكر في كلامه سوى ما يتعلّق به الحكم. وقد يُهْمِلُ المُستفتى فى سؤاله ما يتوقف عليه الجواب الصحيح، ويذكر التفاصيل الأخرى التي لا علاقة لها بالحكم الشرعي، وبعبارة أخرى، يذكر الواقعاتِ الطّرديّة ولا يذكر الواقعات المؤثرة، مثل ما يفعل كثير من العوام عند السؤال عن وقوع الطلاق أنّهم يذكرون واقعات تتعلق بالنزاع بين الزوجين، ولا يذكرون الألفاظ التي استعملت عند إيقاع الطلاق. وحينئذ يجب على المفتى أن يُقيم على السؤال تنقيحات، ويطلب من السائل أن يُجيب عنها على نفس السؤال الذى عرضه على المفتى، ثم يبنى المفتى جوابه على ما تنقّح من صورة المسئلة وربّما يُبين المستفتى بعض يفعل مثل ذلك. وقد لا يتمكن المُستفتى بسبب قلة علمه من أن يُوضح الأمور التي يتوقف عليها معرفةُ الحُكم الشرعي، وحينئذ، ينبغى للمفتى أن يتحقق من تلك الأمور بطرق أخرى. ويقع مثل هذا كثيراً فى الأسئلة عن التعاملات الجارية بين النّاس، فإن المستفتى إنّما يَسْئل عنها حسب فهمه لها، ولا يَعْباً ببعض الأمور المهمة، أو لا يعرف حقيقتها. وقد يُدلس حقيقة المعاملة بتصويرها تصويراً لا يوافق الواقع، فإن فتوى المفتى في مثله إنما تقع على الصُّورة المسئول عنها، ولكنّها تُشهر بالنسبة للتعامل الحقيقي المعروف بين النّاس. ومعروف أنّ الاستفتاء المعروض على الشيخ المرحوم محمد عبده بشأن التأمين التقليدي كان من هذا القبيل، حيث سأله رجل فرنسي اسمه 'موسيو هرسل' بصيغة غير حقيقية، وأظهر أن الموضوع موضوع مُضاربة، فأفتى الشيخ على ذلك الأساس، ثمّ نُشرت الفتوى على نطاق واسع بأنه أجاز التأمين التقليدي. وكذلك وقع فى الهند بحقيقة هذه التعاملات. ولذلك رُوِى عن الإمام محمد رحمه الله تعالى أنّه كان يذهب إلى الصباغين ويسأل عن معاملتهم وما يُديرونها فيما بينهم. وما ذلك إلا لأن يكون على بصيرة من التعاملات الجارية بينهم. وكثيرا ما يُسئَلُ المُفتى فى زماننا عن التعاملات الجارية بين الناس على أساس قانون أو حكم صادر من الحكومة، هل هي جائزة أم لا؟ ويذكرها المُستفتى حسب فهمه لها، ويترك الأمور المهمة التي عليها مدارُ الحُكمِ الشرعي. وينبغى فى مثل هذه الأمور أن يُراجع المفتى ذلك القانون أو الحكم
The ruling depends on (the details), so it is as if he mentioned only what relates to the ruling. The questioner may omit from his question what is necessary for a correct answer, and mention other details that have no relation to the legal ruling. In other words, he mentions incidental facts and does not mention the effective facts, like many common people do when asking about the occurrence of divorce: they mention facts related to the dispute between the spouses, but do not mention the words used when pronouncing divorce. Then the mufti must perform clarifications on the question, and ask the questioner to answer them on the same question he presented to the mufti. Then the mufti builds his answer on the clarified picture of the issue. Perhaps the questioner may explain some important details orally before the mufti, so the mufti should not be satisfied with his statement only, but should [gesture?] to the question to complete it or add that detail, and there is no harm in adding it with his own pen if the questioner asks him to do so. I say: If there is no room to add that detail in the question, then it is also possible for the mufti to begin his answer by stating that the questioner added this detail orally, and if this detail is correct, then the ruling is such. I have often seen my father and my teacher (may Allah have mercy on them) do that. And sometimes the questioner, due to lack of knowledge, cannot clarify the matters on which the knowledge of the legal ruling depends; then the mufti should verify those matters through other means. Such cases occur frequently in questions about current transactions among people, for the questioner asks about them according to his understanding, and does not care about some important matters, or does not know their reality. And sometimes the reality of a transaction is concealed by depicting it in a way that does not match reality. In such a case, the mufti's fatwa falls only on the depicted picture asked about, but it is publicized with respect to the real transaction known among people. It is well-known that the istifta' presented to the late Sheikh Muhammad Abduh regarding conventional insurance was of this kind, where a Frenchman named 'Monsieur Hersel' asked in an unreal form, and made the subject appear as a mudarabah, so the Sheikh gave a fatwa on that basis, then the fatwa was widely published as if he allowed conventional insurance. Similarly, it happened in India where conventional insurance was depicted in an unreal form, then some trusted scholars were asked, and they gave fatwas of permissibility, and those fatwas are still exploited today by some insurance companies. Hence, the mufti of every era must be knowledgeable about the reality of these transactions. Therefore, it is narrated from Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) that he used to go to the dyers and ask about their transactions and what they conduct among themselves. That is only to be insightful about the current transactions among them. And often today the mufti is asked about current transactions among people based on a law or a ruling issued by the government: are they permissible or not? The questioner mentions them according to his understanding, and leaves out the important matters on which the legal ruling revolves. In such matters, the mufti should review that law or ruling.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage from 'Usul al-Ifta' by Muhammad Taqi Usmani discusses the mufti's duty to clarify the question (tanqih al-su'al). The author begins by noting that questioners often omit crucial details while providing irrelevant ones. For example, in divorce cases, people describe the marital conflict but fail to mention the exact words used to pronounce divorce. The mufti must then perform 'tanqihat' (clarifications) by asking the questioner to respond on the same written question, and base his answer on the clarified version. If the questioner provides important details orally, the mufti should note them on the question or, if not possible, mention them in the fatwa that the ruling depends on the oral addition being correct. The author (Usmani) notes that his father and teacher practiced this. The text then warns that some questioners, due to ignorance, cannot properly describe the transaction, or deliberately misrepresent it (e.g., conventional insurance portrayed as mudarabah). The mufti must therefore be aware of real-world practices, like Imam Muhammad who visited dyers to understand their transactions. The passage concludes by advising muftis to review relevant laws or government rulings when asked about them, rather than relying solely on the questioner's description. This lesson is crucial for muftis to avoid issuing fatwas based on incomplete or deceptive presentations.

Key Terms
تنقيحات (tanqihat): Clarifications or probes that the mufti performs on the question to ascertain the relevant facts.
مستفتى (mustafti): The person asking for a fatwa; the questioner.
واقعات مؤثرة (waqi'at mu'aththira): Facts that have legal effect, i.e., are relevant to the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mufti must always clarify the facts behind a question before issuing a fatwa to ensure the ruling is based on the true nature of the case, not just the questioner's incomplete or misleading description.

The Mufti Must Investigate the True Nature of Transactions
Rule on necessity of verifying real transaction before fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of al-tathabbut to identify when a fatwa requires investigating the underlying transaction rather than relying on the asker's description.

Core Idea
A fatwa is only as valid as the reality it addresses—the mufti must investigate the true transaction, not the portrayed one.

Imagine issuing a fatwa based on a false description—only the mufti's ruling is used to legitimize a prohibited practice. This lesson teaches a foundational duty: the mufti must look beyond the questioner's words and uncover the actual transaction and its legal basis. The passage provides cautionary tales and a model from Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Recognize Misrepresentation Risk
Note that the asker may conceal important details or describe the transaction in a way that does not match reality. The fatwa only falls on the picture presented, but it is publicized as applying to the real transaction.
The examples of conventional insurance in Egypt and India show the danger of relying on a false portrayal.
2
Apply the Rule of al-Tathabbut
The mufti must thoroughly investigate the actual transaction. This is a requirement, not a recommendation.
Imam Muhammad personally visited dyers to understand their real transactions, not just their descriptions.
3
Examine Underlying Laws or Regulations
When a transaction is based on a law or government ruling, the mufti must review that law directly before answering.
The example of government employee allowances: the mufti must check for riba or other prohibitions in the law itself.
4
Verify Real Practices
The mufti must be aware of the actual transactions and practices common among people in his time.
This ensures the fatwa addresses the real-world application, not a theoretical abstraction.

With some important matters, or he does not know their reality. And the reality of a transaction may be concealed by portraying it in a way that does not match reality. Indeed, the fatwa of the mufti in such a case only falls on the picture asked about, but it is publicized in relation to the real transaction known among the people. It is known that the istifta presented to the late Shaykh Muhammad Abduh regarding conventional insurance was of this type, because a Frenchman named 'Monsieur Harsel' asked him with an unreal formula and showed that the matter was a mudaraba, so the Shaykh gave a fatwa on that basis, then the fatwa was widely published that he allowed conventional insurance. And that is only so that he may have insight into the current transactions among them. Often a mufti in our time is asked about current transactions among people based on a law or ruling issued by the government: are they permissible or not? The questioner describes them according to his understanding and leaves out the important things on which the legal ruling depends. In such matters, the mufti should review that law or ruling on which the transaction is based before deciding on the answer. For example, if he is asked about what is paid to government employees in a specific country as allowances upon retirement or death, it is necessary before issuing a fatwa on permissibility or impermissibility, and likewise regarding the ruling on whether it is inheritable, to review that law or ruling on which these payments are based, so that it becomes clear whether it includes usury or another legal prohibition, and if it is permissible, whether it is subject to inheritance or not.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage establishes a crucial methodological rule for the mufti: he must ascertain the true nature of the transaction or issue presented to him. The text describes a common problem where the asker either omits important details or deliberately misrepresents the transaction. Two historical examples illustrate the danger: the fatwa of Muhammad Abduh on insurance, which was based on a false premise (mudaraba) and later misused, and a similar incident in India. The rule is then reinforced by the practice of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, who personally studied the dyers' transactions to understand their actual dealings. The passage further instructs that when the transaction is based on a law or government regulation, the mufti must review that law directly rather than relying on the questioner's description. A concrete example is given regarding government employee benefits (allowances upon retirement or death): the mufti must examine the governing law to check for riba or other prohibitions and determine inheritance rules. This rule applies in all eras; the mufti must be fully aware of contemporary practices.

Key Terms
التثبت (al-tathabbut): Thorough verification and investigation of the actual reality of a transaction before issuing a fatwa.
التعامل (al-ta'amul): The actual, real-world transaction or practice occurring among people, as opposed to its description.
المفتى (al-mufti): The person qualified to issue fatwas; he must be knowledgeable and careful in ascertaining facts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text mention the story of Imam Muhammad visiting the dyers?
A) To show that Imam Muhammad was interested in dyeing techniques.
B) To emphasize that a mufti must understand the actual transactions of people firsthand.
C) To prove that dyers were not trustworthy.
D) To discourage muftis from engaging with tradespeople.

Key Takeaway
The mufti's duty is to issue fatwas on realities, not abstractions; he must investigate the actual transaction and its legal basis.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
beginner
6 min
Answer Must Be Based on Explicit Text from the Madhhab
Rule on the mufti's duty to rely on explicit text and delegate when unqualified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Ibn Abideen's rule by determining when a mufti must delegate a fatwa due to lack of explicit text and lack of qualification for istinbat.

Core Idea
A mufti must answer based on explicit madhhab text; if missing and he is not of ahl al-nazar, he must delegate.

In this lesson, we learn a foundational rule of Hanafi fatwa practice: the mufti's answer must be rooted in explicit transmitted rulings from the madhhab. This rule, articulated by Ibn Abideen, clarifies the mufti's responsibility when he cannot directly locate the case in the books. It preserves the integrity of the madhhab by ensuring that only qualified scholars perform independent deduction.

Guided Path
1
Verify the factual picture
The mufti must first understand the exact nature of the case being asked about. Ensure you have the full factual details before searching for a ruling.
This is the first step mentioned in the passage: 'after verification in understanding the picture asked about'.
2
Search for explicit text in madhhab books
Check the standard Hanafi fiqh books for the case either specifically (bi-aynihi) or under a general rule (qā‘ida kulliyya). Ibn Abideen assures that almost every incident is covered.
The mufti's failure to find the text is usually due to lack of familiarity, not absence.
3
If explicit text is found, apply directly
If the case is explicitly mentioned, the mufti must answer accordingly. This is straightforward and requires no further deduction.
The passage says: 'then the matter is easy for the mufti'.
4
If not found, classify under general rulings or maxims
If the case is not explicitly given, the mufti must see if it falls under a broader legal principle or a legal maxim that covers it. This requires scholarly ability (nazar).
Only ahl al-nazar can perform this classification reliably.
5
Delegate if not qualified
If the mufti is not from ahl al-nazar (i.e., lacks capacity for istinbat), he must refer the matter to a more qualified scholar. He cannot issue a fatwa based on his own opinion.
This step preserves the authority of the madhhab and prevents erroneous fatwas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجواب على أساس النقل الصريح

وبعد ما وقع التثبت فى فهم الصُّورة المسئول عنها، فالمهم إدخالها في حكم شرعي ثابت وفى مُعْظَم الأحوالِ تكون المسئلة مذكورة في كتب الفقه بصراحة، فيتعين على المفتى أن يُجيب السائل حسبما جاء في كُتب المذهب، ويتأتى فيه ما أسلفنا من قواعد المفتى نقلاً عن ابن عابدين رسم رحمه الله تعالى. وفي مثل هذا قال ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى: "والغالب أن عدم وجدانه النّص لقلة اطلاعه أو عدم معرفته عدم معرفته بموضع المسئلة المذكورة فيه، إذ قَلَّ ما تقع حادثة إلا ولها ذكر فى كُتب المذهب، إما بعينها، أو بذكر قاعدة كلّيّة تشملها. فإن كانت المسئلة مذكورة بعينها سهل الخطب على المفتى. أما إذا كانت غير مذكورة بعينها، ووقعت الحاجة إلى إدراجها في عموم بعض الأحكام، أو في ضابط فقهي، فإن كان المفتى من غير أهل النظر، وجب عليه أن يُوكل الأمر إلى من هو أعلم منه من أهل النظر والاستنباط.
The answer on the basis of explicit transmitted text. After verification in understanding the picture asked about, the important thing is to bring it under a fixed legal ruling. In most cases, the issue is explicitly mentioned in books of fiqh, so the mufti must answer the questioner according to what is found in the books of the madhhab, and in that applies what we have mentioned earlier of the rules of the mufti, quoting from Ibn Abideen, may Allah have mercy on him. And regarding this, Ibn Abideen said: 'Most often, his not finding the text is due to his lack of familiarity or his not knowing the location of the mentioned issue in it, for rarely does an incident occur except that it has a mention in the books of the madhhab, either specifically or by a general principle that includes it. If the issue is mentioned specifically, then the matter is easy for the mufti. But if it is not mentioned specifically, and there is need to include it under the generality of some rulings or under a legal maxim, then if the mufti is not of the people of independent reasoning, he must delegate the matter to someone more knowledgeable than him from the people of independent reasoning and deduction.'
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage presents the second stage of the fatwa process: after verifying the factual picture, the mufti must apply an established legal ruling. It states that in most cases the issue is explicitly covered in the fiqh books of the madhhab. The mufti is bound to answer according to those texts. The author then quotes Ibn Abideen's famous principle: a mufti's failure to find a text is usually due to lack of familiarity; almost every incident has a textual basis, either directly or via a general rule. If found directly, it is easy. If not, the mufti must incorporate it under broader rulings or a legal maxim. However, if the mufti is not qualified for istinbat (independent deduction), he must refer the matter to a more capable scholar. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on textual authority (naql) and the hierarchy of scholars.

Key Terms
النقل الصريح (al-naql al-sarih): Explicit transmitted textual evidence from the books of the madhhab, either directly or via a general rule.
أهل النظر (ahl al-nazar): Scholars qualified for independent legal reasoning and deduction (ijtihad and istinbat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abideen, what should a mufti do if he cannot find the issue explicitly in the madhhab books and is not qualified for independent deduction?
A) Issue a fatwa based on his own opinion.
B) Refer the matter to a more knowledgeable scholar of istinbat.
C) Reject the question without answering.
D) Apply qiyas without conditions.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must base his fatwa on explicit madhhab text; if the text is not found and he lacks istinbat capacity, he must delegate to a qualified scholar.

The Mufti's Spiritual Preparation: Seeking Divine Guidance Before Ifta'
Instruction on the mufti's conduct before issuing a fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first adab of the mufti before issuing a fatwa and explain its rationale using the practice of the early scholars.

Core Idea
The mufti must seek Allah’s guidance before issuing a fatwa, acknowledging his own inability.

This lesson introduces the first and most fundamental etiquette of the mufti: turning to Allah in supplication before delivering a fatwa. The act of seeking guidance (hidayah) is not merely a formality; it is a recognition that true knowledge and correctness come only from Allah. The passage cites the practice of Makhul and Imam Malik, who would say 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' before giving a fatwa, demonstrating the humility required of one who speaks on behalf of divine law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What is the mufti required to do before issuing a fatwa? Turn to Allah and seek guidance.
The verb used is 'yanbaghi' (it is befitting), indicating a strong recommendation.
2
Note the verbal formulation
What specific phrase did the early scholars use? 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (There is no power and no strength except with Allah).
This phrase acknowledges that all ability comes from Allah.
3
Understand the rationale
Why is this spiritual preparation important? It humbles the mufti and reminds him that his knowledge is insufficient without divine aid.
This prevents arrogance and reduces the risk of error.
4
Connect to Hanafi adab traditions
How does this fit into the broader framework of adab al-ifta? It is the first point, emphasizing sincerity and caution before any fatwa.
Hanafi usul works consistently include this as a foundational adab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الإفتاء
-١ - يَنبغى للمفتى قبل الإفتاء أن يرجع إلى الله سبحانه وتعالى ويسأله الهداية إلى الرشد. قال ابن الصلاح رحمه الله تعالى: "روى عن مكحول ومالك رضى الله عنهما أنهما كانا لا يفتيان حتى يقولا: لاحول ولا قوة إلا بالله."
Etiquette of Ifta':
1 - It is incumbent upon the mufti before issuing a fatwa to turn to Allah Almighty and ask Him for guidance to the right path. Ibn al-Salah, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'It is narrated from Makhul and Malik, may Allah be pleased with them both, that they would not issue a fatwa until they said: There is no power and no strength except with Allah.'
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage introduces the first point of adab (etiquette) for a mufti. The author, Muhammad Taqi Usmani, citing Ibn al-Salah, instructs that before issuing any fatwa, the mufti must turn to Allah in supplication, asking for guidance (هداية) to the correct understanding and ruling. This reflects the mufti's humility and recognition that his knowledge is insufficient without divine assistance. The reference to Makhul (a tabi'i) and Imam Malik shows the practice of the early pious scholars who would verbally acknowledge their reliance on Allah by saying 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (There is no power and no strength except with Allah) before giving a fatwa. This serves as a spiritual preparation, reminding the mufti of his responsibility and the gravity of speaking on behalf of Allah's law. In the Hanafi tradition, this adab is emphasized as a means to prevent error and arrogance. Subsequent points of adab would follow in the original text, but here only the first is presented.

Key Terms
آداب الإفتاء (adab al-ifta): The ethical norms and recommended practices that a mufti should observe before, during, and after issuing a fatwa.
الهداية (al-hidayah): Divine guidance to the correct understanding and ruling in a particular matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 'Allahumma inni a'udhu bika'

Key Takeaway
Before any fatwa, the mufti must humbly seek Allah's guidance, repeating the words of the early imams: 'There is no power and no strength except with Allah.'

Adab of the Mufti: Supplications, Deference, and Caution
Guidelines on mufti's conduct: supplications, deference, and caution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the key etiquettes of the mufti regarding supplications, deference, and caution as outlined in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The mufti must rely on divine guidance, humility, and certainty before issuing any fatwa.

This lesson draws from a classical Hanafi work on Usul al-Iftaa to outline three essential etiquettes for the mufti: the importance of supplication before issuing a fatwa, the duty to defer to more knowledgeable scholars present, and the absolute requirement of being fully certain (tuma'nina) before answering. These principles ensure that fatwas are issued with the utmost care and responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended supplications
The mufti should recite specific Quranic verses and prayers before giving a fatwa, including seeking refuge, asking for knowledge and understanding, and the hadith of guidance in matters of disagreement.
2
Explain the rule of deference
If a more knowledgeable scholar is present, the mufti should refer the question to him unless instructed otherwise.
This shows humility and respect for rank.
3
Understand the condition of tuma'nina
The mufti must not answer unless he is fully confident in the correctness of the answer; any doubt, even slight, must prevent response.
This is the basis for prohibiting fatwa while walking.
4
Apply these etiquettes to a scenario
Given a hypothetical situation, determine the proper conduct of the mufti regarding supplications, deference, and caution.
Integration of all three principles.

" وقال ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى: "حقيق بالمفتى أن يُكثر الدعاء بالحديث الصحيح: اللهم رب جبرئيل وميكائيل وإسرافيل فاطر السماوات والأرض عالم الغيب والشهادة أنت تحكم بين عبادك فيما كانوا فيه يختلفون. اهدني لما اختلف فيه بإذنك، إنك تهدى من تشاء إلى صراط مستقيم. وكان شيخنا (یعنى) العلامة ابن تيمية رحمه الله تعالى كثير الدعاء بذلك. وكانت إذا أشكلت عليه المسائل يقول: يا معلم إبراهيم علمنى، ويُكثر الاستعانة بذلك اقتداءً بمُعاذ بن جبل رضی الله تعالى عنه حيث ث قال لمالك بن يخامرٍ السَّكْسَكِيّ عند موته وقدرآه يبكى فقال والله ما أبكى على دنيا كنت أصيبها منك، ولكن أبكى على العلم والإيمان اللذين كنتُ أتعلّمُهما منك، فقال معاذبن جبل رضى الله تعالى عنه: إنّ العلم والإيمان مكانهما، من ابْتَغاهما وَجَدهما، أطلب العلم عند أربعة عند عويمر أبي الدرداء، وعند عبدالله بن مسعود، و أبي موسى الأشعري، وذكر الرابع. فإن عجز عنه هؤلاء، فسائر أهل الأرض عنه أعجز فعَليْكَ بمُعلّم إبراهيم صلوات الله عليه. . وروى عن سعيد بن المُسَيَّب رحمه الله تعالى أنه كان لا يكاد يُفتى فتيا ولا يقول شيئاً إلا قال: "اللهم سلمنى وسلّم مِنّى . -٢- ينبغي للمفتى أن لا يُبادِرَ بالجواب في مجلس يوجد فيه من هو أعلم منه، بل يحوِّلُ السُّؤال إليه. ويُستثنى منه ما إذا أمره ذلك الرجل الأعلمُ بالجواب فحينئذٍ يُجيب حسب علمه. قال ابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى: "ومن شرائطها حفظه الترتيب والعدل بين المستفتين، لا يميل إلى الأغنياء وأعوان السلطان والأمراء، بل يكتب جواب السابق غنياً كان أو فقيراً. And we recommend to the mufti that with others he should say when he intends to give a fatwa: 'I seek refuge in Allah from the accursed Satan. 'My Lord, expand for me my chest and ease my task and untie the knot from my tongue that they may understand my speech.'
